Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619 Savings promotion programs.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(a): "Prize period" means a period of time, designated by a depository institution, during which a qualifying account holder may submit an entry into the depository institution's savings promotion program for a chance to win a prize designated as the prize for that period.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(b): "Qualifying account" means a savings account that qualifies the savings account holder for an entry into the saving account's depository institution's savings promotion program each time the holder of the savings account:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(b)(i): deposits a minimum amount of money specified by the depository institution into the savings account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(b)(ii): leaves the minimum deposit in the savings account for no less than an amount of time specified by the depository institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(c): "Qualifying account holder" means a person who holds a qualifying account.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(d): "Savings promotion program" means a contest:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(d)(i): that a depository institution conducts to encourage savings deposits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(1)(d)(ii): in which a qualifying account holder is offered a chance to win a designated prize for each entry submitted in association with the qualifying account holder's qualifying account.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2): A depository institution may conduct a savings promotion program if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(a): no qualifying account holder is required to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(a)(i): pay a fee or otherwise provide any consideration to submit an entry in the savings promotion program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(a)(ii): be present at a prize drawing in order to win;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(b): any fee charged by a depository institution in connection with a qualifying account is comparable with a fee charged in connection with a comparable nonqualifying account the depository institution offers;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(c): any interest rate a depository institution associates with a qualifying account is comparable to an interest rate associated with a comparable nonqualifying account the depository institution offers;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(d): each entry in the savings promotion program during a single prize period has an equal chance of winning; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(e): the depository institution:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(e)(i): conducts the savings promotion program in a manner that does not:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(e)(i)(A): jeopardize the depository institution's ability to operate in a safe and sound manner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(e)(i)(B): mislead the depository institution's account holders; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(2)(e)(ii): fully discloses the terms and conditions of the savings promotion program to each of the depository institution's account holders.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(3)(a): require a depository institution that conducts a savings promotion program to maintain all records the commissioner determines necessary for the administration and enforcement of this section; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-619(3)(b): ensure that a depository institution conducts a savings promotion program in accordance with this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702 Interstate acquisition, merger, and branching.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(1): A Utah depository institution or its holding company may acquire control of, acquire all or substantially all the assets of, or merge with:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(1)(a): an out-of-state depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(1)(b): a holding company of an out-of-state depository institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(2): An out-of-state depository institution or its holding company may acquire control of, acquire all or substantially all the assets of, or merge with:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(2)(a): a Utah depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(2)(b): a holding company of a Utah depository institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(3): (3)(a) A Utah depository institution may acquire, through merger or otherwise, a branch of a depository institution in another state without acquiring:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(3)(a): the depository institution in the other state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(3)(b): (3)(a) the charter of the depository institution described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(4): An out-of-state depository institution may acquire, through merger or otherwise, a branch of a depository institution in Utah without acquiring:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(4)(a): the Utah depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(4)(b): the charter of the Utah depository institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(5): (5)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(5)(a): A Utah depository institution may establish a de novo branch in any state that allows de novo interstate branching as described in 12 U.S.C. Secs. 36(g) and 1828(d)(4), as amended.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(5)(b): (5)(c) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(5)(c): An out-of-state depository institution may establish a de novo branch in Utah if the home state of that out-of-state depository institution permits a Utah state chartered depository institution to establish and maintain a de novo branch in that home state under substantially the same terms and conditions as that out-of-state depository institution establishes its de novo branch in Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6): (6)(b); (6)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(a): (6)(b) Any of the following may do anything described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(a)(i): a Utah depository institution or holding company that acquires an out-of-state depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(a)(ii): a Utah depository institution that is the resulting depository institution after merging with an out-of-state depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(a)(iii): a Utah depository institution that otherwise establishes or acquires a branch in a host state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(b): (6)(a) A depository institution or holding company described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(b)(i): continue to operate the out-of-state depository institution or branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(b)(ii): convert any existing main office or branch in the host state into a branch of the Utah  depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(b)(iii): establish or acquire additional branches of the Utah depository institution in any state where the out-of-state depository institution could have done so if the out-of-state depository institution had not been acquired or merged; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(6)(b)(iv): exercise any power and engage in any activity in a host state to the same extent as a depository institution of the same class whose home state is that state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7): (7)(b); (7)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(a): (7)(b) Any of the following may do anything described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(a)(i): an out-of-state depository institution or holding company that acquires a Utah depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(a)(ii): an out-of-state depository institution that is the resulting depository institution after merging with a Utah depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(a)(iii): an out-of-state depository institution that otherwise establishes or acquires a branch in Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(b): (7)(a) A depository institution or holding company described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(b)(i): continue to operate the Utah depository institution or branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(b)(ii): convert any existing main office or branch in Utah into a branch of the out-of-state depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(b)(iii): establish or acquire additional branches of the out-of-state depository institution in any state where the Utah depository institution could have done so if the Utah depository institution had not been acquired or merged; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(7)(b)(iv): exercise any power and engage in any activity in this state to the same extent as a depository institution of the same class whose home state is Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(a): A Utah branch of an out-of-state depository institution shall comply with:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(a)(i): the law of the institution's home state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(a)(ii): the federal law in the case of a federally chartered institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(b): If the laws of this state as a host state conflict with the laws of another state as a home state, the laws of the home state prevail except as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(c): The commissioner may order that Utah law prevails over home state law if the application of Utah law is necessary to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(c)(i): preserve the safe and sound operation of the Utah branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(c)(ii): prevent significant competitive disadvantage to Utah depository institutions in local financial markets; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(c)(iii): otherwise protect the citizens of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(d): The laws of this state regarding community reinvestment, consumer protection, fair lending, and intrastate branching apply to a Utah branch of an out-of-state depository institution to the same extent as those laws apply to a Utah branch of a depository institution chartered by this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(8)(e): An out-of-state depository institution authorized to operate a branch in Utah may underwrite or sell insurance, engage in the direct marketing of securities, or engage in the brokerage of real estate only to the extent permissible for a Utah depository institution of the same class.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(9): (8); (9)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(9)(a): examine, supervise, and regulate an out-of-state depository institution operating or seeking to operate a branch in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(9)(b): (9)(a) take any action or issue any order with regard to a branch described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(10): The acquisition of a charter entitles the acquiring institution to engage in any activity the acquired institution could have engaged in if the acquired institution had not been acquired, so long as the acquiring institution does not convert the acquired institution into, or operate it as, an institution of a different class.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(11): 7-1-703; 7-1-705; 7-1-708
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(11)(a): 7-1-703; 7-1-705; 7-1-708 The activities authorized in this section are subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(11)(a)(i): 7-1-703; 7-1-705 the limitations for mergers and acquisitions set forth in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(11)(a)(ii): 7-1-708 the limitations for branching set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(11)(b): An institution shall file all required applications and receive all appropriate approvals before engaging in any of the activities authorized in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(12): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act An out-of-state depository institution that operates a branch in this state shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-702(12)(a): maintain a certificate of authority to transact business in this state;

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703 Restrictions on acquisition of institutions and holding companies -- Enforcement.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1): 7-1-705; 7-1-705 Unless the commissioner gives prior written approval under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(a): acquire, directly or indirectly, control of a depository institution or depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(b): 7-1-705 vote the stock of a depository institution or depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department acquired in violation of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(c): acquire all or a material portion of the assets of a depository institution or a depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(d): assume all or a material portion of the deposit liabilities of a depository institution subject to the jurisdiction of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(e): take any action that causes a depository institution to become a subsidiary of a depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(f): take any action that causes a person other than an individual to become a depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(g): acquire, directly or indirectly, the voting or nonvoting securities of a depository institution or a depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department if the acquisition would result in the person obtaining more than 20% of the authorized voting securities of the institution if the nonvoting securities were converted into voting securities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(1)(h): merge or consolidate with a depository institution or depository institution holding company subject to the jurisdiction of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(2): A person who willfully violates this section or a rule or order issued by the department under this section is subject to a civil penalty of not more than $1,000 per day during which the violation continues.  The commissioner may assess the civil penalty after giving notice and opportunity for hearing.  The commissioner shall collect the civil penalty by bringing an action in the district court of the county in which the office of the commissioner is located. An applicant for approval of an acquisition is considered to have consented to the jurisdiction and venue of the court by filing an application for approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(3): The commissioner may secure injunctive relief to prevent a change in control or impending violation of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(4): 7-1-705 The commissioner may lengthen or shorten any time period specified in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(5): The commissioner may exempt a class of financial institutions from this section by rule if the commissioner finds the exception to be in the public interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(6): 7-1-705; (6) The prior approval of the commissioner under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(7): (7)(a); (7)(a); Chapter 2, Possession of Depository Institution by Commissioner; Chapter 19, Acquisition of Failing Depository Institutions or Holding Companies; (7)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(7)(a): An out-of-state depository institution without a branch in Utah, or an out-of-state depository institution holding company without a depository institution in Utah, may acquire:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(7)(a)(i): a Utah depository institution only if it has been in existence for at least five years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-703(7)(a)(ii): a Utah branch of a depository institution only if the branch has been in existence for at least five years.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704 Authorization required to engage in business -- Exemptions -- Procedure.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(1): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(1)(a): An institution subject to the jurisdiction of the department may maintain an office in this state or engage in the activities of a financial institution in this state only if it is authorized to do so by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(1)(b): (1) This Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(1)(b)(i): any person who is lawfully engaging in the activities of a financial institution in this state on July 1, 1981, unless the institution was not subject to the jurisdiction of the department before that date;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(1)(b)(ii): an application to establish a branch or additional office; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(1)(b)(iii): the establishment of a service corporation or service organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(2): 7-1-401 An applicant for authorization to become an institution subject to the jurisdiction of the department shall pay to the department the appropriate filing fee, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(2)(a): its undertaking to pay all expenses incurred in conducting any administrative proceedings forming part of the department's consideration of the application;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(2)(b): its proposed articles of incorporation and by-laws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(2)(c): an application in a form prescribed by the commissioner that includes all information the commissioner requires about the source of the proposed original capital and about the identity, personal history, business background and experience, financial condition, and participation in any litigation or administrative proceeding of the organizers, the proposed members of the board of directors, and the principal officers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(2)(d): any other information the commissioner requires.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; 45-1-101 In addition to the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(a): 45-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(a)(i): give notice of the application by publication in three successive issues of a newspaper of general circulation in the county where the principal place of business is to be established; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 give notice of the application by publication as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(b): give notice of the application to other institutions subject to the jurisdiction of the department in a manner and to an extent the commissioner considers appropriate;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c): cause the appropriate supervisor to make a careful investigation and examination of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c)(i): the character, reputation, and financial standing and ability of the organizers;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c)(ii): the character, financial responsibility, experience, and business qualifications of those proposed as officers;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c)(iii): the character and standing in the community of those proposed as directors, principal stockholders, or owners;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c)(iv): the need in the service area where the institution would be located, giving particular consideration to the adequacy of existing financial facilities and the effect the proposed institution would have on existing institutions in the area;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c)(v): the ability of the proposed service area to support the proposed institution, including the extent and nature of existing competition, the economic history and future prospects of the community, and the opportunity for profitable employment of financial institution funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(3)(c)(vi): other facts and circumstances bearing on the proposed institution that the supervisor considers relevant.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(4)(a): The supervisor shall submit findings and recommendations in writing to the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(4)(b): The application, any additional information furnished by the applicant, and the findings and recommendations of the supervisor may be inspected by any person at the department's office, except those portions of the application or report the commissioner declares to be confidential, pursuant to the applicant's request, in order to prevent a clearly unwarranted invasion of privacy.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(5): 45-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(5)(a): 45-1-101 If a hearing is held, the applicant shall publish notice of the hearing at the applicant's expense:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(5)(a)(i): in a newspaper of general circulation within the county where the proposed institution is to be located at least once a week for three successive weeks before the date of hearing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(5)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(5)(b): The notice shall include the date, time, and place of the hearing and any other information required by the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(5)(c): The commissioner shall act on the record before him within 30 days after receipt of the transcript of the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(6): If no hearing is held, the commissioner may, within 90 days of acceptance of the application as complete, approve or disapprove the application based on the papers filed with him, together with the supervisor's findings and recommendations.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a): The commissioner may not approve the application unless the commissioner finds that the applicant has established by the preponderance of the evidence that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(i): in light of the need for financial services in the area, the adequacy of existing facilities, and the effect the proposed institution would have on existing institutions in the area, the public need and convenience will be promoted by the establishment of the proposed institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(ii): in light of the ability of the proposed service area to support the proposed institution, including the extent and nature of existing competition, the economic history and future prospects of the community, and the opportunity for profitable employment of financial institution funds, conditions in the service area in which the proposed institution would transact business afford reasonable promise of a successful operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(iii): the institution is being formed only for legitimate purposes allowed by the laws of this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(iv): the proposed capital equals or exceeds the required minimum and is adequate in light of current and prospective conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(v): if the applicant is seeking authority to accept deposits, the deposits will be insured or guaranteed by an agency of the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(vi): the proposed officers and directors have sufficient experience, ability, and standing to afford reasonable promise of a successful operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(vii): the name of the proposed financial institution does not resemble the name of any other institution transacting business in this state so closely as to cause confusion;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(viii): the applicants have complied with all of the provisions of law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(a)(ix): no properly managed and soundly operated existing institutions offering substantially similar services in the service area to which the application relates will be unduly injured by approval of the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(7)(b): The commissioner may condition approval of the application on the institution's acceptance of requirements or conditions with respect to insurance that the commissioner considers necessary to protect depositors.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(a): The commissioner shall provide written findings and conclusions on the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(b): Upon approving an application, the commissioner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(b)(i): endorse the approval on the articles of incorporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(b)(ii): file one copy with the Division of Corporations and Commercial Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(b)(iii): retain one file copy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(b)(iv): return one copy to the applicant within 10 days after the date of the commissioner's decision approving the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(c): Upon disapproving an application, the commissioner shall mail notice of the disapproval to the applicant within 10 days.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(d): The commissioner may approve an application subject to conditions the commissioner considers appropriate to protect the public interest and carry out the purposes of this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(8)(e): The commissioner shall give written notice of the decision to all persons who have filed a protest to the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(9): Upon approval of an application for authorization to conduct a business subject to the jurisdiction of the department, the commissioner shall issue a license, permit, or other appropriate certificate of authority if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(9)(a): except in the case of credit unions, all of the capital of the institution being formed has been paid in; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(9)(b): all the conditions and other requirements for approval of the application have been met.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(10)(a): Any approval by the commissioner of an application under this section is considered revoked unless the business is open and operating within one year from the date of the approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(10)(b): The commissioner, on written application made before the expiration of that period, and for good cause shown, may extend the date for activation for additional periods not to exceed six months each.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(11): No person may obtain, for the purpose of resale, a certificate of approval to operate any institution under the jurisdiction of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-704(12): (7) The commissioner may approve an application without any notice to other financial institutions to respond to an emergency arising from the insolvency of an existing institution or to prevent the failure of an existing institution if the commissioner makes the findings required by Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705 Approval required for certain transactions -- Application -- Grounds for disapproval.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(1): (5); 7-1-702; 7-1-703; (3) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(1)(a): an application in a form prescribed by the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(1)(b): the fee prescribed for the transaction by the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(1)(c): (3) other information that is required by rule, or that the commissioner considers necessary to make the findings required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(1)(d): if the applicant is not a Utah resident, a Utah corporation, or an out-of-state corporation qualified to do business in this state, a written consent to service of process on a resident of this state in any action or suit arising out of or connected with the proposed action.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(2)(a): Within 60 days of acceptance of the application as complete, the commissioner shall respond to the application by writing the commissioner's findings of fact, conclusions, and order.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(2)(b): The commissioner may approve an application subject to the terms and conditions  the commissioner considers necessary to protect the public interest and carry out the purposes of this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(2)(c): The commissioner may defer acceptance of the application as complete until the applicant has provided any information the commissioner considers necessary to decide whether to approve or deny the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3): The commissioner may disapprove any application filed under this section if  the commissioner finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3)(a): the proposed transaction would be detrimental to the safety and soundness of the applicant, to any institution that is a party to the transaction, or to a subsidiary or affiliate of that institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3)(b): the applicant, its executive officers, directors, or principal stockholders have not established a record of sound performance, efficient management, financial responsibility, and integrity so that it would be against the interest of the depositors, other customers, creditors, or shareholders of an institution, or the public to authorize the proposed transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3)(c): the financial condition of the applicant or any other institution that is a participant in the proposed transaction might jeopardize the financial stability of the applicant or other institution, or prejudice the interests of depositors or other customers of the applicant or other institutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3)(d): the consummation of the proposed transaction will tend to substantially lessen competition, unless the commissioner finds that the anticompetitive effects of the proposed transaction are clearly outweighed by the benefit of meeting the convenience and needs of the relevant market area to be served;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3)(e): the applicant has not established a record of meeting the credit needs of the communities that it or its subsidiary depository institution serves; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(3)(f): in the case of an interstate transaction, the applicant fails to obtain any required approval from a federal or state agency with regulatory authority over any of the institutions participating in the transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(4): In the case of an interstate transaction, the commissioner may accept an application in the form and manner prescribed by the state or federal agency that primarily regulates the applicant, supplemented as necessary to enable the commissioner to decide whether to approve or deny the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(5): 7-1-708; 7-1-708
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(5)(a): 7-1-708 The following branching activities, if they do not involve a merger or acquisition, are not subject to the requirements of this section, but are subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(5)(a)(i): the establishment of a branch in Utah or another state by an out-of-state depository institution with a previously established branch in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(5)(a)(ii): the establishment of a branch in another state by a Utah depository institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-705(5)(b): 7-1-708 Other interstate branching activities are subject to the requirements of both this section and Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706 Application to commissioner to exercise power -- Procedure -- Notice.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(1): 7-1-704; 7-1-705 Except as provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(1)(a): issue any rule or order;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(1)(b): exercise any powers granted to the commissioner under this title; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(1)(c): act on any matter that is subject to the approval of the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(2): Within 10 days of receipt of the request, the commissioner shall, at the applicant's expense, cause a supervisor to make a careful investigation of the facts relevant or material to the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(3)(a): The supervisor shall submit written findings and recommendations to the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(3)(b): The application, any additional information furnished by the applicant, and the findings and recommendations of the supervisor may be inspected by any person at the office of the commissioner, except those portions of the application or report that the commissioner designates as confidential to prevent a clearly unwarranted invasion of privacy.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(4): 63G-30-102; (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(4)(a): 63G-30-102 If a hearing is held concerning the request, the commissioner shall publish notice of the hearing, at the applicant's expense, for the county where the applicant is located, as a class A notice under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(4)(b): (4)(a) The notice required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(4)(c): The commissioner shall act upon the request within 30 days after the close of the hearing, based on the record before the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(a): If no hearing is held, the commissioner shall approve or disapprove the request within 90 days of receipt of the request based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(a)(i): the application;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(a)(ii): additional information filed with the commissioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(a)(iii): the findings and recommendations of the supervisor.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(b): The commissioner shall act on the request by issuing findings of fact, conclusions, and an order, and shall mail a copy of each to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(b)(i): the applicant;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(b)(ii): all persons who have filed protests to the granting of the application; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(5)(b)(iii): other persons that the commissioner considers should receive copies.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(6): The commissioner may impose any conditions or limitations on the approval or disapproval of a request that the commissioner considers proper to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(6)(a): protect the interest of creditors, depositors, and other customers of an institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(6)(b): protect its shareholders or members; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-706(6)(c): carry out the purposes of this title.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-708(1): A Utah depository institution or an out-of-state depository institution with a Utah branch or seeking to acquire a branch in this state may establish one or more branches, or relocate a branch office or its main office in this state, subject to the prior approval of the commissioner.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-708(8): An out-of-state depository institution with a branch in Utah is not subject to the requirements of this section if the office or branch to be established or relocated is located outside of Utah.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709 Branches -- Discontinuance of operation.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(1): A Utah depository institution or out-of-state depository institution authorized to do business in this state may discontinue operation of a branch upon resolution of its board of directors.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(2): Upon adopting the resolution, the institution shall file an application with the commissioner specifying:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(2)(a): the location of the branch to be discontinued;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(2)(b): the date of the proposed discontinuance;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(2)(c): the reasons for closing the branch; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(2)(d): the extent to which the public need and convenience or service to members would still be adequately met.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(3): 45-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(3)(a): 45-1-101 Upon filing its application with the commissioner, the institution shall publish notice of the discontinuance:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(3)(a)(i): in a newspaper serving the area once a week for two consecutive weeks; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(3)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(3)(b): The commissioner may approve the application after a reasonable comment period following publication.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-709(4): An out-of-state depository institution with a branch in Utah is not subject to the requirements of this section if the branch to be closed is located outside of Utah.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710 "Agency" defined -- Purposes and establishment of agency.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(1): 7-1-608; 7-1-609 As used in this section, "agency" means a place, person, or facility, stationary or mobile, other than the home office or a branch office:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(1)(a): where functions of the financial institution not involving the receiving or paying of deposits, making of loans or the handling of cash may be performed;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(1)(b): established for individual transactions and for special temporary purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(1)(c): 7-1-608; 7-1-609 established for the purposes set forth in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(1)(d): established to perform the functions of a financial institution service corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(2): A financial institution may establish one or more agencies without the prior written approval of the commissioner.  Within 30 days of the establishment of an agency, the financial institution shall inform the commissioner in writing of the address of the agency and the specific functions for which it was established.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-710(3): 7-1-708 No agency may be converted to a branch without compliance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-711 Mobile facilities -- Approval required for operation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No financial institution may operate a mobile facility in this state at which deposits are received, checks paid, or money lent without the prior written approval of the commissioner.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-712 Acquisition of office of another financial institution.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any financial institution authorized to do business in this state may acquire an office of any other financial institution located in this state upon obtaining the prior written approval of the commissioner in the manner provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-713 Conversion of financial institution -- Approval required -- Procedure -- Federal-state conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-713(1): 7-1-706 Any financial institution authorized to do business as a particular class of financial institution under any chapter of this title may convert to an institution authorized to do business under another chapter by applying to the department for approval in the manner provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-713(2): If the commissioner approves the conversion, the institution shall immediately surrender its former charter to the commissioner. Under its new charter as a financial institution of a different class, it is entitled to all the benefits and powers conferred under the applicable chapter to other financial institutions of that class and is subject to examination, supervision, and regulation to the same extent as all other financial institutions of that class.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-713(3): Any depository institution organized under the laws of this state may convert to a depository institution organized under the laws of the United States upon compliance with the laws of the United States and upon surrender of its charter to the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-713(4): 7-1-706 Any depository institution organized under the laws of the United States or any other state that is authorized to do business in this state may convert into a depository institution subject to the jurisdiction of the department by applying to the department for approval in the manner provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714 Judicial review of acts of commissioner -- Hearing by court.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(1): Any person aggrieved by any rule, regulation, order, decision, or ruling or other act or failure to act of the commissioner under this title is entitled to judicial review.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(2): Judicial review of other agency actions shall be governed by the procedures and requirements of this subsection.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(2)(a): Within 30 days after receipt of notice of a rule, order, or other decision or ruling not arising from an adjudicative proceeding, or within 120 days after the commissioner has failed to act upon a request or application, the aggrieved person may file an application for judicial review with a court of competent jurisdiction in the county in which the applicant is located, or in the county where the office of the commissioner is located, and may request an immediate hearing on the act or failure to act.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(2)(b): The court shall require adequate notice to be served on the commissioner and all other interested parties and shall give the petition for review precedence on its calendar.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(2)(c): The court shall review the record before the commissioner and shall adjudicate the question, enter appropriate orders, and enforce them.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(2)(d): The court may declare void any rule, regulation, order, decision, ruling, or other act of the commissioner it finds to be arbitrary, capricious, an abuse of discretion, or otherwise contrary to law.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-714(3): Any action for judicial review of acts or failure to act of the commissioner shall be heard by the court and shall be based on the record made before the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715 Loan production offices -- Application and procedure for approval.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(1): With the prior approval of the commissioner, a  depository institution may establish one or more loan production offices.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(2): A loan production office shall be staffed and accessible to the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3): A loan production office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(a): solicit loans on behalf of its depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(b): assemble credit information;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(c): make property inspections and appraisals;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(d): secure title information;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(e): prepare applications for loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(f): solicit investors to purchase loans from the depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(g): seek to have these investors contract with a depository institution for servicing the loans; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(3)(h): engage in other activities in the nature of acting as an agent for the parent depository institution in facilitating the production of loans.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(4): A loan production office may not do any of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(4)(a): accept deposits;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(4)(b): originate deposit, savings, or share accounts;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(4)(c): pay checks;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(4)(d): approve loans; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(4)(e): disburse loan funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(5): A loan processed by a loan production office may only be approved at the main office or approved branch of the depository institution, except a loan production office may make a recommendation, subject to independent analysis and approval by the depository institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(6): Funds from a loan processed by a loan production office may only be disbursed at the main office or approved branch of the depository institution, or at the office of an independent third party, such as a title company or escrow agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(7): 7-1-708 Although a loan production office is not considered a branch, the establishment of a loan production office is subject to the prior approval of the commissioner in the manner provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(8): Each depository institution with operating loan production offices in Utah as of June 1, 1994, shall file an initial registration with the department stating the location of each loan production office on or before July 15, 1994. All subsequent applications for a loan production office require prior approval of the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-715(9): 7-1-401 If the commissioner determines that it is in the public interest, the department may examine the books and records of the office at the per diem charge established in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716 Affiliate depository institutions acting as agents -- Notification required.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(1): Any depository institution may, at its main office or at any branch, act as an agent of any other depository institution that is a subsidiary of the same depository institution holding company in conducting the activities authorized under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(2): This section applies regardless of whether the affiliate depository institutions have the same home state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(3): 7-1-715 A depository institution acting as agent for an affiliate depository institution may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(3)(a): receive deposits;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(3)(b): renew time deposits;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(3)(c): 7-1-715 engage in the activities authorized for a loan production office under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(3)(d): service loans; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(3)(e): receive payments on loans and other obligations.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(4): A depository institution may not do any of the following as an agent on behalf of an affiliate depository institution:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(4)(a): open or originate deposit, savings, or share accounts;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(4)(b): evaluate or approve loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(4)(c): disburse loan funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(4)(d): conduct any activity as an agent that it is prohibited from conducting as a principal under any applicable law.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(5): A depository institution acting as a principal may not have an affiliate depository institution act as its agent in conducting any activity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(5)(a): the principal depository institution is prohibited from conducting; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(5)(b): the agent depository institution would be prohibited from conducting as a principal.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(6): An agency relationship between affiliates under this section shall be consistent with safe and sound practices and shall comply with all applicable law.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-716(7): A depository institution acting as an agent is not considered to be a branch of the affiliate solely because of activities conducted under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-801 False statement derogatory to financial condition of depository institution a misdemeanor -- Exemptions.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-801(1): Any person who willfully and knowingly makes or circulates or transmits to another any statement or rumor, written, printed, or by word of mouth, which is untrue in fact and is directly or by inference derogatory to the financial condition or standing of any depository institution, or who knowingly counsels, aids, procures, or induces another to state, transmit, or circulate any such statement or rumor, is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-802(4)(f): 7-1-304; 7-1-320; 7-1-322; Chapter 2, Possession of Depository Institution by Commissioner; Chapter 19, Acquisition of Failing Depository Institutions or Holding Companies to any court in a proceeding under:

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-802(6)(e)(ii)(B): undue speculation in securities or currency markets.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803 Conflicting interests of commissioner, supervisors, and examiners -- Loans and accounts -- Disclosure -- Penalty.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(1): Neither the commissioner nor any supervisor or examiner may do any of the following with respect to any institution under the supervision of the department:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(1)(a): be indebted, directly or indirectly, as a borrower, accommodation endorser, surety, or guarantor to an institution, or to an individual or any other legal or commercial entity owning or controlling an institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(1)(b): be an officer, director, or employee of any institution or of an individual or any other legal or commercial entity owning or controlling an institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(1)(c): own or deal in, directly or indirectly, the shares or obligations of an institution or of a corporation owning or controlling an institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(1)(d): receive, directly or indirectly, from an institution or any officer, director, or employee of an institution, any salary, fee, or compensation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(1)(e): be interested in or engage in the negotiations of any loan to, obligation of, or accommodation for another person to or with an institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2): (1) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(a): have and maintain savings, transaction, share, time deposit, or other accounts, or certificates and deposits in any financial or depository institution in the state, or be a lessee of a safe deposit box on the same terms and conditions available to the public generally;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(b): be indebted to a depository institution under the supervision of the department on terms offered to the public generally upon:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(b)(i): a mortgage loan upon the mortgagor's own home;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(b)(ii): an open or closed end consumer loan granted before the person became employed with the department or before the institution became subject to the jurisdiction of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(b)(iii): in the case of a supervisor or examiner, a consumer loan lawfully made prior to January 1, 1991, provided that while the debt is subject to the provisions of this chapter, the terms of the debt are not changed in favor of the debtor in a manner not offered and provided to other creditworthy borrowers or waived or extended as a result of delinquency or default; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(b)(iv): a debt fully secured at all times by deposits in the institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(c): be indebted on an installment debt transferred to an institution under the jurisdiction of the department in the regular course of business by a seller of consumer goods; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(2)(d): continue to receive payments under a regularly established pension plan of general application for fully retired employees of an institution under the supervision of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(3): (2) Full disclosure in writing of any indebtedness incurred under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-803(4): Any person who knowingly violates this section with the intention of getting gain through the influence of his office shall forfeit  the office or employment and is guilty of a third degree felony.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-806 Money market funds arranging with bank to honor two-party instruments -- Discouraging payment of interest to two persons on funds in transit -- Pyramiding and similar schemes as misdemeanors.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this act shall be construed to prevent money market funds from making arrangements with banks to honor two party checks, drafts, or other instruments.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-807 Printed checks, drafts and orders -- Requirements -- Violation as misdemeanor.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Every check, draft, order, or other like instrument printed for a customer of any institution issuing transaction accounts in the state as part of a series after the effective date of this act shall have on its face the name and address of the account holder, the month and year the account was opened, and the number of the check, draft, order, or other like instrument in unbroken, sequential, numerical order, beginning with the number 101, except for initial deposits to open a new account or in case of lost or stolen checks when a limited supply of unnumbered counterchecks may be issued. Any person who violates this section is guilty of a class C misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808 Closing days for depository institutions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(1): Depository institutions shall be closed to the general public on Sundays.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a): The commissioner may designate any additional or different day on which depository institutions are closed to the general public, such as in the event of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(i): an emergency;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(ii): disaster;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(iii): flood;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(iv): earthquake;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(v): fire;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(vi): power outage;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(vii): heavy snow;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(viii): other impediment to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(viii)(A): business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(viii)(B): the safety of customers and employees; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(a)(ix): any circumstance in which closing on an additional or different day serves the public interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(2)(b): (2)(a) The commissioner may designate a day under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(3)(a): A depository institution may elect to be open or closed to the general public during business hours of its choosing on any day not designated under this section as a day for closing.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-808(3)(b): A depository institution shall provide adequate notice to its customers or members of any change from normal business hours.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-809 Articles of incorporation -- Amended or restated articles of incorporation -- Prerequisites to filing.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-809(1): The Division of Corporations and Commercial Code may not file articles of incorporation that state that the purpose of the corporation is to transact business as a depository institution or to hold a corporation that will transact business as a depository institution until the department certifies that it has reviewed and does not object to the articles of incorporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-809(2): (1); 7-1-705 A corporation whose articles of incorporation have been filed with the Division of Corporations and Commercial Code pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-809(3): The Division of Corporations and Commercial Code may not file articles of amendment or articles of restatement of a depository institution or depository institution holding company until the department has certified that it has reviewed and does not object to the articles of amendment or articles of restatement.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001 Definitions -- Written consent or court order for disclosure by financial institution -- Exception.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1): As used in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(a): "Account holder" means a person for whom an account is held by a financial institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b): "Governmental entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i): the state, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(A): a department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(B): an institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(C): a board;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(D): a division;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(E): a bureau;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(F): an office;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(G): a commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(H): a committee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(i)(I): an elected official; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii): a political subdivision of the state, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(A): a county;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(B): a city;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(C): a town;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(D): a school district;

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(F): a redevelopment agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(G): a special improvement district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(b)(ii)(H): a taxing district.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(c): "Nonprotected record" means a record maintained by a financial institution to facilitate the conduct of the financial institution's business regarding a person or account, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(c)(i): the existence of an account;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(c)(ii): the opening and closing dates of an account;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(c)(iii): the name under which an account is held; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(c)(iv): the name, address, and telephone number of an account holder.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(d): "Protected record" means a record that is not defined as a nonprotected record.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(e): "Record" means information that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(e)(i): prepared, owned, received, or retained by a financial institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(e)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(e)(ii)(A): inscribed on a tangible medium; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(e)(ii)(B): stored in an electronic or other medium; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(1)(e)(iii): retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(2): 7-1-1006(1) Except for a governmental entity listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(2)(a): written permission from all account holders of the account referenced in the record to be examined; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(2)(b): an order from a court of competent jurisdiction permitting access to the record.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1001(3): This section does not apply to a review made by the commissioner to determine whether a financial institution is operating in accordance with law.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1003 Intervention to challenge or stay order -- Burden on governmental entity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1003(1)(b): stay compliance with the order.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-1-1003(2): Upon intervention, the burden shall be on the governmental entity obtaining the order to show that there is reasonable cause for the issuance of the order.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1 Supervisory actions by commissioner -- Grounds -- Mergers or acquisitions authorized by commissioner -- Possession of business and property taken by commissioner.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1): Chapter 19, Acquisition of Failing Depository Institutions or Holding Companies; 7-1-307; 7-1-308; 7-1-313 An institution under the jurisdiction of the department is subject to supervisory actions by the commissioner under this chapter or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(a): the institution is not in a safe and sound condition to transact its business;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(b): an officer of the institution or other person has refused to be examined or has made false statements under oath regarding its affairs;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(c): the institution or other person has violated its articles of incorporation or any law, rule, or regulation governing the institution or other person;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(d): the institution or other person is conducting its business in an unauthorized or unsafe manner, or is practicing deception upon its depositors, members, or the public, or is engaging in conduct injurious to its depositors, members, or the public;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(e): the institution or other person has been notified by its primary account insurer of the insurer's intention to initiate proceedings to terminate insurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(f): the institution or other person has failed to maintain a minimum amount of capital as required by the department, any state, or the relevant federal regulatory agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(g): the institution or other person is a depository institution that has failed or refused to pay its depositors in accordance with the terms under which the deposits were received, or has or is about to become insolvent;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(h): the institution or other person or its officers or directors have failed or refused to comply with the terms of a legally authorized order issued by the commissioner or by any federal authority or authority of another state having jurisdiction over the institution or other person;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(i): the institution or other person or its officers or directors have failed or refused, upon proper demand, to submit its records, books, papers, and affairs for inspection to the commissioner or to a supervisor or an examiner of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(j): the institution or other person or its officers or directors, after 30 days written notice, have failed to comply with or have continued to violate this title or any rule or regulation of the department issued under it;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-1(1)(k): any person who controls the institution or other person subject to the jurisdiction of the department has used the control to cause the institution or other person to be or about to be in an unsafe or unsound condition, to conduct its business in an unauthorized or unsafe manner, or to violate this title or any rule or regulation of the department issued under it; or

Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2 Jurisdiction of district court -- Supervision of actions of commissioner in possession -- Authority of commissioner and court.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(1): Chapter 19, Acquisition of Failing Depository Institutions or Holding Companies The district court for the county in which the principal office of the institution or other person is situated has jurisdiction in the liquidation or reorganization of the institution or other person of which the commissioner has taken possession under this chapter or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2): Before taking possession of an institution or other person under his jurisdiction, or within a reasonable time after taking possession of an institution or other person without court order, as provided in this chapter, the commissioner shall cause to be commenced in the appropriate district court, an action to provide the court supervisory jurisdiction to review the actions of the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(3): The actions of the commissioner are subject to review of the court.  The court has jurisdiction to hear all objections to the actions of the commissioner and may rule upon all motions and actions coming before it.  Standing to seek review of any action of the commissioner or any receiver or liquidator appointed by him is limited to persons whose rights, claims, or interests in the institution would be adversely affected by the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(4): The authority of the commissioner under this chapter is of an administrative and not judicial receivership.  The court may not overrule a determination or decision of the commissioner if it is not arbitrary, capricious, fraudulent, or contrary to law.  If the court overrules an action of the commissioner, the matter shall be remanded to the commissioner for a new determination by him, and the new determination shall be subject to court review.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2 Action to review the commissioner's actions -- Supervision of actions of commissioner in possession -- Authority of commissioner and court.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(1): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration Before taking possession of an institution or other person under the commissioner's jurisdiction, or within a reasonable time after taking possession of an institution or other person without court order, as provided in this chapter, the commissioner shall bring an action in a court with jurisdiction under
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2)(a): The actions of the commissioner are subject to review of the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2)(b): The court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2)(b)(i): hear all objections to the actions of the commissioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2)(b)(ii): rule upon all motions and actions coming before the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(2)(c): Standing to seek review of any action of the commissioner or any receiver or liquidator appointed by the commissioner is limited to persons whose rights, claims, or interests in the institution would be adversely affected by the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(3)(a): The authority of the commissioner under this chapter is of an administrative and not judicial receivership.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(3)(b): The court may not overrule a determination or decision of the commissioner if it is not arbitrary, capricious, fraudulent, or contrary to law.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-2(3)(c): If the court overrules an action of the commissioner, the matter shall be remanded to the commissioner for a new determination by the commissioner, and the new determination shall be subject to court review.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3 Action for injunction against commissioner in possession -- Procedure -- Appeal.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1)(a): Whenever any institution or other person of which the commissioner has taken possession considers itself aggrieved by the taking, it may within 10 days after the taking apply to the court to enjoin further proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1)(b): After ordering the commissioner to show cause why further proceedings should not be enjoined and after hearing the allegations and proofs of the parties and determining the facts, the court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1)(b)(i): dismiss the application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1)(b)(ii): enjoin the commissioner from further proceedings if the court finds the taking to be arbitrary, capricious, an abuse of discretion, or otherwise contrary to law.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1)(c): If the court enjoins further proceedings, it shall order the commissioner to surrender possession of the institution in a manner and on terms designated by the court in the public interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(1)(d): Notice of any hearings shall be given to persons designated by the court in the manner designated by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-3(2): 7-2-9 An appeal may be taken by the commissioner, a receiver, or liquidator appointed by the commissioner under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-4 Consent required for institution to resume business.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The institution or other person may resume business only with the consent of and upon conditions approved by the commissioner. The commissioner may give his consent to resumption of business if arrangements have been made by the institution or its stockholders, by reorganization or otherwise, to the satisfaction of the commissioner, to pay all creditors of the institution, aside from the stockholders, and to remedy the default or condition for which possession was taken and to pay the expenses of the proceeding.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-5 Appointment of receiver or assignment for creditors -- Notice required -- Commissioner taking possession.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No receiver may be appointed by any court and no deed or assignment for the benefit of creditors may be filed in any district court within this state for any institution or other person under the jurisdiction of the commissioner, except upon notice to the commissioner, unless because of urgent necessity the court determines that it is necessary to do so to preserve the assets of the institution. The commissioner may within five days after service of the notice upon him take possession of the institution, in which case no further proceedings shall be had upon the application for the appointment of a receiver or under the deed of assignment, or, if a receiver has been appointed or the assignee has entered upon the administration of his trust, the appointment shall be vacated or the assignee shall be removed upon application of the commissioner to the court by which the receiver was appointed or in which the assignment was filed, and the commissioner shall proceed to administer the assets of the institution as provided in this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-5 Appointment of receiver or assignment for creditors -- Notice required -- Commissioner taking possession.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-5(1): A receiver may not be appointed by any court and a deed or assignment for the benefit of creditors may not be filed in a court within this state for any institution or other person under the jurisdiction of the commissioner, except upon notice to the commissioner, unless because of urgent necessity the court determines that it is necessary to do so to preserve the assets of the institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-5(2): The commissioner may, within five days after service of the notice upon the commissioner, take possession of the institution, in which case no further proceedings shall be had upon the application for the appointment of a receiver or under the deed of assignment, or, if a receiver has been appointed or the assignee has entered upon the administration of his trust, the appointment shall be vacated or the assignee shall be removed upon application of the commissioner to the court by which the receiver was appointed or in which the assignment was filed, and the commissioner shall proceed to administer the assets of the institution as provided in this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6 Possession by commissioner -- Notice -- Presentation, allowance, and disallowance of claims -- Objections to claims.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(a): Possession of an institution by the commissioner commences when notice of taking possession is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(a)(i): posted in each office of the institution located in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(a)(ii): delivered to a controlling person or officer of the institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(b): All notices, records, and other information regarding possession of an institution by the commissioner may be kept confidential, and all court records and proceedings relating to the commissioner's possession may be sealed from public access if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(b)(i): the commissioner finds it is in the best interests of the institution and its depositors not to notify the public of the possession by the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(b)(ii): the deposit and withdrawal of funds and payment to creditors of the institution is not suspended, restricted, or interrupted; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(1)(b)(iii): the court approves.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2): 63G-30-102; 45-1-101; 7-2-15; (9); (2)(d)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(a): 63G-30-102; 45-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(a)(i): Within 15 days after taking possession of an institution or other person under the jurisdiction of the department, the commissioner shall publish a notice to all persons who may have claims against the institution or other person to file proof of their claims with the commissioner before a date specified in the notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(a)(ii): The filing date shall be at least 90 days after the date of the first publication of the notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(a)(iii): 63G-30-102; 45-1-101 The notice shall be published:

Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(b)(i): Within 60 days of taking possession of a depository institution, the commissioner shall send a similar notice to all persons whose identity is reflected in the books or records of the institution as depositors or other creditors, secured or unsecured, parties to litigation involving the institution pending at the date the commissioner takes possession of the institution, and all other potential claimants against the institution whose identity is reasonably ascertainable by the commissioner from examination of the books and records of the institution.  No notice is required in connection with accounts or other liabilities of the institution that will be paid in full or be fully assumed by another depository institution or trust company.  The notice shall specify a filing date for claims against the institution not less than 60 days after the date of mailing.  Claimants whose claims against the institution have been assumed by another depository institution or trust company pursuant to a merger or purchase and assumption agreement with the commissioner, or a federal deposit insurance agency appointed as receiver or liquidator of the institution, shall be notified of the assumption of their claims and the name and address of the assuming party within 60 days after the claim is assumed.  Unless a purchase and assumption or merger agreement requires otherwise, the assuming party shall give all required notices.  Notice shall be mailed to the address appearing in the books and records of the institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(b)(ii): Inadvertent or unintentional failure to mail a notice to any person entitled to written notice under this paragraph does not impose any liability on the commissioner or any receiver or liquidator appointed by him beyond the amount the claimant would be entitled to receive if the claim had been timely filed and allowed.  The commissioner or any receiver or liquidator appointed by him are not liable for failure to mail notice unless the claimant establishes that it had no knowledge of the commissioner taking possession of the institution until after all opportunity had passed for obtaining payment through filing a claim with the commissioner, receiver, or liquidator.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(c): Upon good cause shown, the court having supervisory jurisdiction may extend the time in which the commissioner may serve any notice required by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(d): 7-2-15; (9) The commissioner has the sole power to adjudicate any claim against the institution, its property or other assets, tangible or intangible, and to settle or compromise claims within the priorities set forth in Section

All claims against the institution shall be filed with the receiver or liquidator within the applicable time specified in this section and the receiver or liquidator shall adjudicate the claims as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(2)(f): The procedure established in this section is the sole remedy of claimants against an institution or its assets in the possession of the commissioner.

For the purpose of this subsection only, late filed claims may be allowed if proof was filed before the final distribution of assets of the institution to claimants of the same priority and are payable only out of the remaining assets of the institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(5)(b): A late filed claim may be disallowed under any other provision of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-2-6(6): Debts owing to the United States or to any state or its subdivisions as a penalty or forfeiture are not allowed, except for the amount of the pecuniary loss sustained by the act, transaction, or proceeding out of which the penalty or forfeiture arose.
