Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 5 - Trust Business
**********************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1 Definitions -- Allowable trust companies -- Exceptions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1): (1)(c); 75-1-201(55); Title 61, Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act; Chapter 22, Regulation of Independent Escrow Agents; Title 75, Chapter 3, Part 5, Supervised Administration; Title 13, Chapter 21, Credit Services Organizations Act; 7-1-103(8) As used in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(a): "Business trust" means an entity engaged in a trade or business that is created by a declaration of trust that transfers property to trustees, to be held and managed by them for the benefit of persons holding certificates representing the beneficial interest in the trust estate and assets.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(b): (1)(c); 75-1-201(55) "Trust business" means, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c): Title 61, Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act; Chapter 22, Regulation of Independent Escrow Agents; Title 75, Chapter 3, Part 5, Supervised Administration; Title 13, Chapter 21, Credit Services Organizations Act "Trust business" does not include the following means of holding money, assets, or other property:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(i): money held in a client trust account by an attorney authorized to practice law in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(ii): Title 61, Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act money held in connection with the purchase or sale of real estate by a person licensed as a principal broker in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(iii): Chapter 22, Regulation of Independent Escrow Agents money or other assets held in escrow by a person authorized by the department in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(iv): money held by a homeowners' association or similar organization to pay maintenance and other related costs for commonly owned property;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(v): money held in connection with the collection of debts or payments on loans by a person acting solely as the agent or representative or otherwise at the sole direction of the person to which the debt or payment is owed, including money held by an escrow agent for payment of taxes or insurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(vi): money and other assets held in trust on an occasional or isolated basis by a person who does not represent that the person is engaged in the trust business in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(vii): money or other assets found by a court to be held in an implied, resulting, or constructive trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(viii): Title 75, Chapter 3, Part 5, Supervised Administration money or other assets held by a court appointed conservator, guardian, receiver, trustee, or other fiduciary if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(viii)(A): Title 75, Chapter 3, Part 5, Supervised Administration the conservator, receiver, guardian, trustee, or other fiduciary is responsible to the court in the same manner as a personal representative under
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(viii)(B): the conservator, trustee, or other fiduciary is a certified public accountant or has qualified for and received a designation as a certified financial planner, chartered financial consultant, certified financial analyst, or similar designation suitable to the court, that evidences the conservator's, trustee's, or other fiduciary's professional competence to manage financial matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(ix): Title 13, Chapter 21, Credit Services Organizations Act money or other assets held by a credit services organization operating in compliance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(x): money, securities, or other assets held in a customer account in connection with the purchase or sale of securities by a regulated securities broker, dealer, or transfer agent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(c)(xi): money, assets, and other property held in a business trust for the benefit of holders of certificates of beneficial interest if the fiduciary activities of the business trust are merely incidental to conducting business in the business trust form.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(d): 7-1-103(8) "Trust company" means an institution authorized to engage in the trust business under this chapter.  Only the following may be a trust company:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(d)(i): a Utah depository institution or its wholly owned subsidiary;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(d)(ii): an out-of-state depository institution authorized to engage in business as a depository institution in Utah or its wholly owned subsidiary;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(d)(iii): 7-1-103(8) a corporation, including a credit union service organization, owned entirely by one or more federally insured depository institutions as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(d)(iv): a direct or indirect subsidiary of a depository institution holding company that also has a direct or indirect subsidiary authorized to engage in business as a depository institution in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(1)(d)(v): any other corporation continuously and lawfully engaged in the trust business in this state since before July 1, 1981.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(2): Only a trust company may engage in the trust business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(3): The requirements of this chapter do not apply to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(3)(a): an institution authorized to engage in a trust business in another state that is engaged in trust activities in this state solely to fulfill its duties as a trustee of a trust created and administered in another state;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(3)(b): a national bank, federal savings bank, federal savings and loan association, or federal credit union authorized to engage in business as a depository institution in Utah, or any wholly owned subsidiary of any of these, to the extent the institution is authorized by its primary federal regulator to engage in the trust business in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-1(3)(c): a state agency that is otherwise authorized by statute to act as a conservator, receiver, guardian, trustee, or in any other fiduciary capacity.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2 Permit required to engage in trust business -- Exceptions.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2(1): No trust company shall accept any appointment to act in any agency or fiduciary capacity, including that of personal representative, executor, administrator, conservator, guardian, assignee, receiver, depositary, or trustee under order or judgment of any court or by authority of any law of this state or as trustee for any purpose permitted by law or otherwise engage in the trust business in this state, unless and until it has obtained from the commissioner a permit to act under this chapter.  This provision does not apply to any bank or other corporation authorized to engage and lawfully engaged in the trust business in this state before July 1, 1981.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2(2): Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act; Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act; Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act; Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act; Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act Nothing in this chapter prohibits:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2(2)(a): Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act; Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act any corporation organized under
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2(2)(b): Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act any corporation organized under
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2(2)(c): Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act; Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act any corporation organized under
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-2(2)(d): any depository institution from holding in an agency or fiduciary capacity individual retirement accounts or Keogh plan accounts established under Section 401(a) or 408(a) of Title 26 of the United States Code.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3 Application for authorization to engage in trust business -- Criteria for granting -- Authority of trust company.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(1): 7-1-704; 7-1-401 A person seeking authorization to become a trust company and engage in the trust business in this state shall file an application with the commissioner in the manner provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2): The commissioner shall, in deciding whether or not to approve the application, take into account:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(a): the character and condition of the applicant's assets;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(b): the adequacy of its capital;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(c): its earnings record;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(d): the quality of its management;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(e): the qualifications of any person proposed to be an officer in charge of the trust operations;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(f): the needs of the community for fiduciary services;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(g): the volume of business that the applicant will probably do; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(2)(h): any other relevant facts and circumstances, including the availability of legal counsel to advise and pass upon matters relating to the trust business.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(3): The commissioner may not apply criteria making it more difficult for a state chartered depository institution to obtain approval to engage in the trust business than for a federally chartered depository institution of the same class.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(4): The commissioner may impose such conditions when authorizing a person to engage in the trust business as he considers appropriate to protect the public interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-3(5): Upon receiving authorization from the commissioner to become a trust company and engage in the trust business, the trust company is qualified to act as fiduciary in any capacity without bond.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-4 Withdrawal from trust business.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Any trust company which desires to withdraw from and discontinue doing a trust business shall furnish to the commissioner satisfactory evidence of its release and discharge from all the obligations and trusts undertaken by it, and after the company has furnished that evidence the commissioner shall revoke his certificate of authority to do a trust business previously issued to that trust company, and thereafter that trust company may not be permitted to use and may not use the word "trust" in its corporate name or in connection with its business, nor undertake the administration of any trust business.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5 Revocation of trust authority -- Procedure.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(a): The commissioner may issue and serve upon a trust company a notice of intent to revoke the authority of the trust company to exercise the powers granted by this chapter, if, in the commissioner's opinion, the trust company:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(a)(i): is unlawfully or unsoundly exercising the powers granted under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(a)(ii): has unlawfully or unsoundly exercised the powers granted under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(a)(iii): has failed, for a period of five consecutive years, to exercise the powers granted by this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(a)(iv): fails or has failed to comply with requirements upon which its permit is conditioned; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(a)(v): fails or has failed to comply with any rule of the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(b): The notice shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(b)(i): contain a statement of the facts constituting the alleged unlawful or unsound exercise of powers, or failure to exercise powers, or failure to comply; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(1)(b)(ii): fix the time and place at which a hearing will be held to determine whether an order revoking authority to execute those powers should issue against the trust company.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(2)(a): If the trust company or its representative does not appear at the hearing, the commissioner may consider the trust company to be in default, and may issue a revocation order.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(2)(b): If default has occurred, or if upon the record made at any hearing the commissioner finds that any allegation specified in the notice of charges has been established, the commissioner shall issue and serve upon the trust company an order:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(2)(b)(i): prohibiting it from accepting any new or additional trust accounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(2)(b)(ii): revoking its authority to exercise any powers granted under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(2)(c): Any order issued under this section permits the trust company to continue to service all previously accepted trust accounts pending their expeditious divestiture or termination.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-5(3): 7-1-714 A revocation order shall become effective 30 days after service of the order upon the trust company and shall remain effective and enforceable, unless it is stayed, modified, terminated, or set aside by action of the commissioner or by judicial review as provided for in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-6 Confidentiality of communications and writings concerning trust -- Actions to protect property or authorized under probate laws not precluded.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any trust company exercising the powers and performing the duties described in this chapter shall keep inviolate all communications and writings made to or by that trust company relating to the existence, condition, management or administration of any agency or fiduciary account confided to it and no creditor or stockholder of any such trust company shall be entitled to disclosure or knowledge of any such communication or writing, except that the directors, president, vice president, manager, treasurer, and trust officers, and any employees assigned to work on the trust business, and the attorney or auditor employed by it shall be entitled to knowledge of any such communication or writing and except that in any suit or proceeding relating to the existence, condition, management or administration of the account, the court in which the suit is pending may require disclosure of any such communication or writing.  A trust company is not, however, precluded from filing an action in court to protect trust account property or as authorized under

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7 Management and investment of trust money.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(1): Money received or held by a trust company as agent or fiduciary, whether for investment or distribution, shall be invested or distributed as soon as practicable as authorized under the instrument creating the account and may not be held uninvested any longer than is reasonably necessary.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(2): Title 75, Utah Uniform Probate Code If the instrument creating an agency or fiduciary account contains provisions authorizing the trust company, its officers, or its directors to exercise their discretion in the matter of investments, money held in the trust account under that instrument may be invested only in those classes of securities which are approved by the directors of the trust company or a committee of directors appointed for that purpose.  If a trust company acts in any agency or fiduciary capacity under appointment by a court of competent jurisdiction, it shall make and account for the investments according to
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(3)(a): Money received or held as agent or fiduciary by any trust company which is also a depository institution, whether for investment or distribution, may be deposited in the commercial department or savings department of that trust company to the credit of its trust department.  Whenever the money so deposited in a fiduciary or managing agency account exceed the amount of federal deposit insurance applicable to that account, the trust company shall deliver to the trust department or put under its control collateral security as outlined in Regulation 9.10 of the Comptroller of the Currency.  However, if the instrument creating such a fiduciary or managing agency account expressly provides that money may be deposited to the commercial or savings department of the trust company, then the money may be so deposited without setting aside collateral securities as required under this section and the deposits in the event of insolvency of any such trust company shall be treated as other general deposits are treated.  A trust company that deposits trust funds in its commercial or savings department shall be liable for interest on the deposits only at the rates, if any, paid by the trust company on deposits of like kind not made to the credit of its trust department.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(3)(b): Money received or held as agent or fiduciary by a trust company, whether for investment or distribution, may be deposited in an affiliated depository institution.  Whenever the money so deposited in a fiduciary or managing agency account exceed the amount of federal deposit insurance applicable to that account, the depository institution shall deliver to the trust company or put under its control collateral security as outlined in Regulation 9.10 of the Comptroller of the Currency.  However, if the instrument creating the fiduciary or managing agency account expressly permits money to be deposited in the affiliated depository institution, the money may be so deposited without setting aside collateral securities as required under this section and deposits in the event of insolvency of the depository institution shall be treated as other general deposits are treated.  A trust company that deposits trust money in an affiliated depository institution is liable for interest on the deposits only at the rates, if any, paid by the depository institution on deposits of like kind.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(4): 75-7-813; 75-7-814; Title 75, Utah Uniform Probate Code In carrying out all aspects of its trust business, a trust company shall have all the powers, privileges, and duties as set forth in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-7(5): Nothing in this section may alter, amend, or limit the powers of a trust company acting in a fiduciary capacity as specified in the particular instrument or order creating the fiduciary relationship.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-8 Segregation of trust assets -- Books and records required -- Examination -- Trust property not subject to claims or debts against trust company.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A trust company exercising the powers to act as an agent or fiduciary under this chapter shall segregate all assets held in any agency or fiduciary capacity from the general assets of the company and shall keep a separate set of books and records showing in proper detail all transactions engaged in under authority of this chapter.  These books and records shall be open to inspection by the commissioner and shall be examined by him or by examiners appointed by him as provided in

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-9(1): 75-1-201 A trust company may cause any security, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-9(2): The records of the trust company shall at all times show the ownership of any such investment, which investment shall be in the possession or control of the trust company and be kept separate and apart from the assets of the trust company.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-11 Self-dealing with trust property -- Own stock as trust property -- Policies for dealing with trust securities.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-11(1): 7-5-7; Title 75, Utah Uniform Probate Code Except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-11(2): A trust company may retain and vote stock of the trust company or of any of its affiliates received by it as assets of any trust account or in any other fiduciary relationship of which it is appointed agent or fiduciary, unless the instrument creating the relationship otherwise provides.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-11(3): Every trust company shall adopt written policies and procedures regarding decisions or recommendations to purchase or sell any security to facilitate compliance with federal and state securities laws.  These policies and procedures, in particular, shall prohibit the trust company from using material inside information in connection with any decision or recommendation to purchase or sell any security.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-12 Directors' audit of trust business -- Report available to commissioner or examiners -- Examinations in lieu of audit.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A committee of the board of directors, exclusive of any active officers of the trust department, of every trust company authorized to engage in the trust business in this state shall, at least once during a 15-month period, make a suitable audit of the trust business operations of the institution or cause a suitable audit to be made by auditors responsible only to the board of directors and shall ascertain whether the trust business operations of the institution have been administered in accordance with law and sound fiduciary principles. A report of the audit, together with the action taken thereon, shall be made available to the commissioner, his examiners, or the examiners of other trust company regulating agencies upon request. An examination by the state or other trust company regulating agencies or both made during the same period may be substituted for this audit.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13 Collective investment funds.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(1): A person authorized to engage in the trust business in this state may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(1)(a): establish collective investment funds that authorize participation by fiduciary or trust accounts of the trust company, its affiliates, or both; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(1)(b): participate in collective investment funds established by an affiliate of the trust company, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(1)(b)(i): the affiliate is authorized under the laws of its chartering authority to establish a collective investment fund in which its affiliates may participate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(1)(b)(ii): the plan establishing the collective investment fund specifically authorized the participation.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(2): Funds held by a trust company may be invested collectively in a collective investment fund in accordance with the rules prescribed by the appropriate governmental regulatory agency or agencies, if this investment is not specifically prohibited under the instrument, judgment, decree, or order creating the regulatory relationship.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(3): Unless ordered to do so by a court of competent jurisdiction, a trust company operating collective investment funds is not required to render a court accounting with regard to those funds; but it may, by application to the district court, secure approval of such an accounting on such conditions as the court may establish.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(4): This section applies to all relationships in existence on  or after May 1, 1989.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-13(4): This section applies to all relationships in existence on or after May 1, 1989.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14 Mergers, consolidations, acquisitions, transfers, or reorganizations involving entities engaged in trust business -- Succession of rights and duties -- Petition for appointment of another trust company.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(a)(ii): a depository institution; or

Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(b)(i): the creation by a trust company of a subsidiary corporation that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(b)(i)(A): wholly owned by that trust company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(b)(i)(B): organized solely for the purpose of conducting all or any portion of the trust business of that trust company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(b)(ii): any merger or other combination between a trust company and:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(b)(ii)(A): a wholly owned trust company subsidiary of that trust company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(1)(b)(ii)(B): a wholly owned trust company subsidiary of the depository institution holding company which owns or controls that trust company.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2): 7-1-702; 7-1-704; 7-1-705 Notwithstanding any provision of law to the contrary, an eligible trust company may, subject to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(i): merge or consolidate with another eligible trust company;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(ii): acquire control of another eligible trust company;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(iii): acquire all or a portion of the assets and trust business of another eligible trust company;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(iv): assume all or any portion of the liabilities of another eligible trust company;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(v): transfer control to another eligible trust company;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(vi): transfer all or a portion of its assets and trust business to another eligible trust company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(a)(vii): transfer all or a portion of its liabilities to another eligible trust company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(2)(b): reorganize.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(3): (3)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(3)(a): (3)(b) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-5-14(3)(b): Except as provided otherwise in the relevant trust instrument, any interested person may, not more than 30 days after receipt of written notice of the merger, consolidation, acquisition, transfer, or reorganization, petition any court of competent jurisdiction to appoint another or succeeding trust company with respect to any agency or fiduciary relationship affecting that interested person, and until another or succeeding trust company is so appointed, the acquiring or resulting trust company is entitled to act as agent or fiduciary with respect to the agency or fiduciary relationship.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5 Acquisition of own stock restricted -- Capital requirements.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(1): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(1)(a): An industrial bank may not accept as collateral, or be a purchaser of, shares of its own capital stock, unless taking the shares as collateral or purchasing them is necessary to prevent loss upon a debt previously contracted in good faith.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(1)(b): (1) All shares of stock acquired under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(1)(c): The par value of all the shares held after acceptance or purchase may not exceed 10% of the capital and surplus of the industrial bank.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(2)(a): Each industrial bank accepting or holding deposits shall maintain the minimum amount of capital required by its federal deposit insurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(2)(b): The commissioner may require a greater amount of capital if the commissioner determines that it is necessary to protect the interests of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(2)(b)(i): the depositors and other customers of the industrial bank; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-5(2)(b)(ii): the public.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-7 Reports to commissioner.
----------------------------------------------------
Each industrial bank shall file reports of its condition  in accordance with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-11 Dividends.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-11(1): The board of directors of an industrial bank may declare a dividend out of the net profits of the industrial bank after providing for all expenses, losses, interest, and taxes accrued or due from the industrial bank in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-11(2): The industrial bank shall transfer to a surplus fund at least 10% of its net profits before dividends for the period covered by the dividend, until the surplus reaches 100% of its capital stock.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-11(3): Any amount paid from the industrial bank's net earnings into a fund for the retirement of any debenture capital or preferred stock for the period covered by the dividend is considered an addition to its surplus fund if, upon the retirement of the debenture capital or preferred stock, the amount paid into the retirement fund for the period may be properly carried to the surplus fund of the industrial bank.  In this case the industrial bank shall transfer to the surplus fund the amount paid into the retirement fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-13 Real estate acquisition, holding, and conveyance.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An industrial bank may purchase, hold, and convey real estate, other than premises used in the conduct of its business, only for the purposes and in a manner prescribed by rule.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-14 Investment in property used in conduct of business.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-14(1): An industrial bank may invest in premises, equipment, and other property used in conducting its own business, as the board of directors may approve by resolution.  This property may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-14(1)(a): real property and any interest in real property, furniture, fixtures, and equipment for use in carrying on its own business; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-14(1)(b): the stock, bonds, debentures, or other obligations of any subsidiary or affiliate whose exclusive activity is the ownership and management of property used in conducting the industrial bank's business.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-14(2): The amount of these investments may not exceed 50% of the industrial bank's total capital, unless the commissioner approves a higher amount in writing.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-15 Bad debts.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-15(1): All demand and matured debts due to any industrial bank on which interest is past due and has not been paid for a period of six months, unless they are well secured and in the process of collection, are considered bad debts and shall be charged off to the profit and loss account.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-15(2): The industrial bank shall maintain in its files documentation to support its evaluation of the security and monthly reports of its collection efforts and a plan of collection.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16 Registration of industrial bank holding company -- Filing and contents of statement -- Exemptions -- Rules.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(1): Each industrial bank holding company shall register with the department by filing a registration statement in a form prescribed by the commissioner.  The statement shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(1)(a): the name, address, and principal occupation of each officer and director of the registrant;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(1)(b): a statement of financial condition as of a date not more than six months prior to the date of registration;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(1)(c): a certificate of good standing in the state in which the registrant is incorporated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(1)(d): evidence that the company is authorized to transact business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(2): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(2)(a): (1) A person may not form an industrial bank holding company, unless it:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(2)(a)(i): is authorized to do so by the commissioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(2)(a)(ii): (1) is registered with the department as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(2)(b): An applicant for authorization to form a holding company shall file an application in a form prescribed by the commissioner by rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(3): 7-1-502 The commissioner may exempt an industrial bank holding company in whole or in part from registration if it is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(3)(a): a bank holding company or savings and loan holding company subject to federal regulation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(3)(b): a person that is a holding company only because the person owns or controls voting shares of an industrial bank or holding company acquired in connection with the underwriting of securities if the person holds these shares no longer than 120 days, unless the commissioner approves a longer period to permit their sale on a reasonable basis;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(3)(c): 7-1-502 a person exempt from the jurisdiction of the department under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(3)(d): a person exempted in writing by the commissioner or by rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-16(4): The commissioner may adopt rules with respect to industrial bank holding companies as are necessary to protect:

Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-19 Meetings of the board of directors.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-19(1): A quorum of the board of directors of each industrial bank shall meet at least once each quarter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-19(2): Minutes of each meeting of the board of directors shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-19(2)(a): kept by the secretary of the industrial bank; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-19(2)(b): maintained at the head office of the industrial bank.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20 Limitations on loans to one borrower -- Exceptions -- Rules.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(1): Except as provided in this section, the total loans and extensions of credit, including credit exposure to a derivative transaction, by an industrial bank to a person outstanding at any one time may not exceed 15% of the industrial bank's total capital.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(2): (1) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (1) The commissioner may by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(3)(a): (1) exempt from Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(3)(b): define terms and phrases necessary to interpret and implement this section;

Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(3)(d): describe records required to be maintained;

Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-20(3)(f): prescribe other actions necessary to interpret and implement this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21 Application of chapter to industrial loan companies.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(1): As used in this section, "industrial loan company" is a person that on March 17, 2004, is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(1)(a): authorized to conduct business under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(1)(b): not authorized to hold or receive deposits.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(2): (2)(a)(i); (ii); 7-1-701(3); (2)(a)(i); (ii) An industrial loan company may operate as an industrial bank under this chapter except that the industrial loan company:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(2)(a): may not hold or receive deposits without:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(2)(a)(i): the prior written approval of the commissioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(2)(a)(ii): obtaining insurance from the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation or a successor federal deposit insurance entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(2)(b): (2)(a)(i); (ii) may not engage in any conduct authorized by this title that is conditioned on the industrial loan company being a depository institution without meeting the conditions described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(2)(c): 7-1-701(3); (2)(a)(i); (ii) may not use a term listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-8-21(3): If a person is not authorized to conduct business under this chapter on March 17, 2004, that person may not be considered an industrial loan company under this section.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 9 - Utah Credit Union Act
*****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-1 Title.
----------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Credit Union Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-2 Description of credit unions.
---------------------------------------------------------
A credit union is a cooperative, nonprofit association, incorporated under this chapter to encourage thrift among its members, to create sources of credit at fair and reasonable rates of interest, and to provide an opportunity for its members to use and control their resources on a democratic basis in order to improve their economic and social condition.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3 Definitions.
----------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a): "Association" means a group of persons that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a)(i): constitute the members of a formal association organized for:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a)(i)(A): an identifiable interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a)(i)(B): an identifiable purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a)(i)(C): a specific profession; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a)(i)(D): a specific occupation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(a)(ii): are employed by a common employer.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(b): "Association" does not include a group of persons that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(b)(i): identified or created primarily on the basis of a relationship between any person and:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(b)(i)(A): a consumer;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(b)(i)(B): a customer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(b)(i)(C): a client; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(1)(b)(ii): created primarily for the purpose of expanding the membership in a credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(2): "Capital and surplus" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(2)(a): shares;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(2)(b): deposits;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(2)(c): reserves; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(2)(d): undivided earnings.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(3): "Corporate credit union" means any credit union organized pursuant to any state or federal act for the purpose of serving other credit unions.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(4): 7-9-59(2) "Credit union service organization" means an entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(4)(a): 7-9-59(2) that provides any of the services listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(4)(b): in which a credit union organized under this chapter holds an ownership interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(5): "Deposits" means that portion of the capital paid into the credit union by members on which a specified rate of interest will be paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(6): 7-9-51; 7-9-53 "Field of membership" means persons designated as eligible for credit union membership in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(6)(a): 7-9-51; 7-9-53 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(6)(b): the bylaws of the credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(7): "Immediate family" means parents, spouse, surviving spouse, children, and siblings of the member.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(a): "Member-business loan" means any loan, line of credit, or letter of credit, the proceeds of which will be used for:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(a)(i): a commercial purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(a)(ii): other business investment property or venture purpose; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(a)(iii): an agricultural purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b): "Member-business loan" does not include an extension of credit:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(i): that is fully secured by a lien on a one- to four- family dwelling that is the primary residence of a member;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(ii): that is fully secured by:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(ii)(A): shares or deposits in the credit union making the extension of credit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(ii)(B): deposits in other financial institutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(iii): the repayment of which is fully insured or fully guaranteed by, or where there is an advance commitment to purchase in full by, an agency of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(iii)(A): the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(iii)(B): a state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(iii)(C): a political subdivision of a state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(8)(b)(iv): that is granted by a corporate credit union to another credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(9): 7-9-55 "Nonexempt credit union" means a credit union that is a nonexempt credit union under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(10): "Share drafts," "deposit drafts," and "transaction accounts" mean accounts from which owners are permitted to make withdrawals by negotiable or transferable instruments or other orders for the purpose of making transfers to other persons or to the owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-3(11): "Shares" means that portion of the capital paid into the credit union by members on which dividends may be paid.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5 Powers of credit unions.
----------------------------------------------------
In addition to the powers specified elsewhere in this chapter and subject to any limitations specified elsewhere in this chapter, a credit union may:Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(1): make contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(2): sue and be sued;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(3): acquire, lease, or hold fixed assets, including real property, furniture, fixtures, and equipment as the directors consider necessary or incidental to the operation and business of the credit union, but the value of the real property may not exceed 7% of credit union assets, unless approved by the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(4): pledge, hypothecate, sell, or otherwise dispose of real or personal property, either in whole or in part, necessary or incidental to its operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(5): incur and pay necessary and incidental operating expenses;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(6): require an entrance or membership fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7): receive the funds of its members in payment for:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(a): shares;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(b): share certificates;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(c): deposits;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(d): deposit certificates;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(e): share drafts;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(f): NOW accounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(7)(g): other instruments;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(8): allow withdrawal of shares and deposits, as requested by a member orally to a third party with prior authorization in writing, including drafts drawn on the credit union for payment to the member or any third party, in accordance with the procedures established by the board of directors, including drafts, third-party instruments, and other transaction instruments, as provided in the bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(9): charge fees for its services;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(10): extend credit to its members, at rates established in accordance with the bylaws or by the board of directors;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(11): extend credit secured by real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12): (12)(b); (12)(a); 7-9-58
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(a): (12)(b) subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(a)(i): other credit unions;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(a)(ii): credit union service organizations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(a)(iii): other financial organizations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(b): (12)(a); 7-9-58 make co-lending arrangements, including loan participation arrangements, in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(b)(i): the credit union or credit union service organization that originates a loan for which co-lending arrangements are made shall retain an interest of at least 10% of the loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(b)(ii): on or after May 5, 2003, the originating credit union or credit union service organization may sell to a credit union an interest in a co-lending arrangement that involves a member-business loan only if the person receiving the member-business loan is a member of the credit union to which the interest is sold;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(b)(iii): on or after May 5, 2003, the originating credit union or credit union service organization may sell to a credit union service organization an interest in a co-lending arrangement that involves a member-business loan only if the person receiving the member-business loan is a member of a credit union that holds an interest in the credit union service organization to which the interest is sold; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(12)(b)(iv): 7-9-58 a nonexempt credit union may not originate, participate in, or obtain any interest in a co-lending arrangement, including a loan participation arrangement, in violation of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(13): sell and pledge eligible obligations in accordance with written policies of the board of directors;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(14): engage in activities and programs of the federal government or this state or any agency or political subdivision of the state, when approved by the board of directors and not inconsistent with this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(15): act as fiscal agent for and receive payments on shares and deposits from the federal government, this state, or its agencies or political subdivisions not inconsistent with the laws of this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(16): borrow money and issue evidence of indebtedness for a loan or loans for temporary purposes in the usual course of its operations;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(17): discount and sell notes and obligations;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(18): sell all or any portion of its assets to another credit union or purchase all or any portion of the assets of another credit union;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(19): invest funds as provided in this title and in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(20): maintain deposits in insured depository institutions as provided in this title and in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(21): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(21)(a): hold membership in corporate credit unions organized under this chapter or under other state or federal statutes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(21)(b): hold membership or equity interest in associations and organizations of credit unions, including credit union service organizations;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(22): declare and pay dividends on shares, contract for and pay interest on deposits, and pay refunds of interest on loans as provided in this title and in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(23): collect, receive, and disburse funds in connection with the sale of negotiable or nonnegotiable instruments and for other purposes that provide benefits or convenience to its members, as provided in this title and in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(24): make donations for the members' welfare or for civic, charitable, scientific, or educational purposes as authorized by the board of directors or provided in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(25): act as trustee of funds permitted by federal law to be deposited in a credit union as a deferred compensation or tax deferred device, including individual retirement accounts as defined by Section 408, Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(26): purchase reasonable accident and health insurance, including accidental death benefits, for directors and committee members through insurance companies licensed in this state as provided in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(27): provide reasonable protection through insurance or other means to protect board members, committee members, and employees from liability arising out of consumer legislation including truth-in-lending and equal credit laws and as provided in its bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(28): reimburse directors and committee members for reasonable and necessary expenses incurred in the performance of their duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(29): participate in systems which allow the transfer, withdrawal, or deposit of funds of credit unions or credit union members by automated or electronic means and hold membership in entities established to promote and effectuate these systems, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(29)(a): the participation is not inconsistent with the law and rules of the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(29)(b): any credit union participating in any system notifies the department as provided by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(30): issue credit cards and debit cards to allow members to obtain access to their shares, deposits, and extensions of credit;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(31): provide any act necessary to obtain and maintain membership in the credit union;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(32): exercise incidental powers necessary to carry out the purpose for which a credit union is organized;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(33): undertake other activities relating to its purpose as its bylaws may provide;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(34): engage in other activities, exercise other powers, and enjoy other rights, privileges, benefits, and immunities authorized by rules of the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(35): act as trustee, custodian, or administrator for Keogh plans, individual retirement accounts, credit union employee pension plans, and other employee benefit programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(36): advertise to the general public the products and services offered by the credit union if the advertisement prominently discloses that to use the products or services of the credit union a person is required to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(36)(a): be eligible for membership in the credit union; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-5(36)(b): become a member of the credit union.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6 Formation of corporation to conduct credit union -- Approval of commissioner.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act; Chapter 1, General Provisions
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(a): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act; Chapter 1, General Provisions Ten or more incorporators belonging to the same group of 200 persons or more having a field of membership may, with the approval of the commissioner, form a corporation to conduct a credit union under:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(a)(i): this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(a)(ii): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(a)(iii): Chapter 1, General Provisions
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(b): This chapter takes precedence over conflicting provisions of other state law governing:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(b)(i): the formation of the corporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(b)(ii): the duties and obligations of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(b)(ii)(A): the corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(b)(ii)(B): the corporation's officers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(1)(b)(ii)(C): the corporation's shareholders or members.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(2): (1) The commissioner may grant the approval referenced in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(2)(a): the proposed field of membership is favorable to the success of the credit union;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(2)(b): the standing of the proposed membership will give assurance that its affairs will be administered in accordance with this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(2)(c): the proposed credit union has a reasonable promise of financial viability; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(2)(d): formation of the credit union would not result in a substantial adverse financial impact on an existing credit union having the same or substantially the same field of membership.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(3): (3)(b); (1); (2); 7-1-704; (3)(a); 7-1-704(3); 7-9-45(2)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(3)(a): (3)(b); (1); (2); 7-1-704 Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(3)(b): (3)(a); 7-1-704(3); 7-9-45(2) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(3)(b)(i): 7-1-704(3) if the proposed credit union has a field of membership that does not base eligibility on residence in a county, the persons seeking formation of the proposed credit union are not required to provide the notice required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-6(3)(b)(ii): 7-9-45(2) a credit union may not be required to obtain federal insurance if the credit union complies with Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-7 Forms furnished by commissioner.
------------------------------------------------------------
The commissioner shall furnish all forms and blanks necessary for the formation of the credit union.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-9 Amendment of articles of incorporation.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-9(1): The articles of incorporation may be amended at meetings of the shareholders called for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-9(2): A notice of a meeting called for that purpose shall be given by mailing a copy thereof to each member at least 10 days prior to the date of the meeting or by giving notice as provided by the articles of incorporation and the bylaws of the credit union. Notice of meetings shall contain the proposed amendment.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-9(3): A three-fourths vote of all members present shall be necessary to amend the articles.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-9(4): No amendment shall be made without the approval of the commissioner.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-10 Filing amendment.
----------------------------------------------
The Division of Corporations and Commercial Code shall accept for filing an amendment to the articles of incorporation if it finds that the amendment conforms to law and has been approved by the commissioner.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-11 Bylaws and amendments to be approved.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-11(1): A credit union may not receive payments on shares, deposits, or certificates, or make any loans or other transactions, until its bylaws have been approved in writing by the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-11(2): An amendment to a credit union's bylaws does not become operative until the amendment to the bylaws is approved by the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-11(3): 7-9-52(1); 7-9-52
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-11(3)(a): 7-9-52(1); 7-9-52 If the amendment to the bylaws of a credit union expands the field of membership of a credit union as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-11(3)(b): If the bylaws or an amendment to the bylaws of a credit union adds an association to the field of membership of the credit union, the commissioner may require that the credit union provide written confirmation from the association that the association has agreed to be served by the credit union.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12 Contents of bylaws.
------------------------------------------------
The bylaws of a credit union shall specify at least the following:Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(1): the name of the credit union;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(2): the purpose for which the credit union was formed;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(3): 7-9-51; 7-9-53 a field of membership of the credit union that complies with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(4): the number of directors and procedures for their election;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(5): the term of directors;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(6): whether a credit manager, credit committee, or combination of both shall be responsible for credit functions of the credit union;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(7): the duties of the officers;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(8): the time of year of the annual meeting of members;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(9): the manner in which members shall be notified of meetings;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(10): the number of members which shall constitute a quorum at meetings;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(11): the manner of amending;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(12): the manner in which officers may act as surety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-12(13): such other matters, rules, and regulations as the board of directors consider necessary.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-13 Fiscal year.
-----------------------------------------
The fiscal year of the credit union shall end at the close of business on December 31 of each year.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-14 Meetings.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-14(1): The annual meeting of the credit union shall be held at such time and place as the bylaws prescribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-14(2): Special meetings may be held as the bylaws prescribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-14(3): Notice of all meetings of the credit union shall be given as the bylaws prescribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-14(4): In the absence of any provisions in the bylaws, special meetings of the members of the credit union may be called by a majority of the members of the corporation.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-15 Appeals from board of directors or committees.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Appeals from decisions of the board of directors, supervisory committee, or credit committee shall be made as the bylaws prescribe.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16 Members -- Eligibility -- Liability -- Grounds for closing account -- Denial of membership.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(1): A person within the field of membership of a credit union may be admitted to membership, upon:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(1)(a): payment of any required entrance or membership fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(1)(b): payment for one or more shares; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(1)(c): compliance with this chapter and the bylaws of the credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(2): A member who is eligible for membership in a credit union at the time the member is admitted as a member but who is no longer in the field of membership of the credit union may retain membership in the credit union unless otherwise provided in the bylaws of the credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(3): A member of the credit union may not be held personally or individually liable for payment of the credit union's debts.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(4): The credit union may close the account of any member whose actions have resulted in any financial loss to the credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-16(5): Denial of membership is not considered a denial of credit.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17 Membership officer -- Appointment -- Eligibility -- Function -- Appeals from.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17(1): One or more membership officers may be appointed by the board of directors.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17(2): A membership officer may approve applications for membership under conditions prescribed by the board of directors and the bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17(3): A membership officer shall be appointed from among the members of the credit union.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17(4): A president, vice president, or loan officer may not serve as a membership officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17(5): The membership officer authorized to approve membership shall submit to the board of directors at each monthly meeting a list of approved or pending applications for membership received since the previous monthly meeting, and other related information as the board or the bylaws may require.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-17(6): A person denied membership by a membership officer may appeal the denial to the board of directors.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-18 Expulsion of member.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-18(1): The board of directors or board-designated representatives may expel from the credit union any member who has not carried out his engagements with the credit union, or neglected or refused to comply with the credit union board policies, provisions of this chapter, or of the credit union bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-18(2): If the member whose expulsion is under consideration is a member of the board of directors or credit committee, the supervisory committee shall call a special meeting of the members to hear the facts and act upon the proposed expulsion.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-19 Payments to expelled members -- Liability of member not relieved by expulsion.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-19(1): Except in the case of liquidation or dissolution, the amount paid in on shares or deposited by members who have been expelled shall be paid to them with all accrued interest, in the order of expulsion.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-19(2): Payment shall be made only as funds become available.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-19(3): All amounts due the credit union by the expelled member shall be deducted by the credit union before any amounts are paid to the expelled member.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-19(4): Expulsion does not relieve a member from any liability to the credit union.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20 Board of directors -- Powers and duties -- Loan limitations.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(1): At annual meetings the members shall elect from their number a board of directors consisting of an odd number of not less than five members.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(2): The bylaws may provide balloting by:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(2)(a): mail;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(2)(b): ballot box; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(2)(c): both mail and ballot box.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(3): Voting may not be by proxy.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(4): A member of the board of directors shall hold office for the term prescribed in the bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(5): The board of directors shall meet at least monthly.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(6): (7); (8) The board of directors shall have the general management of the affairs, funds, and records of the credit union.  In particular, the board of directors shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(6)(a): act upon an application for membership;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(6)(b): act upon expulsion of a member;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(6)(c): fix the amount of surety bond required of each officer or employee having custody of funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-9-20(6)(d): determine the rate of interest or dividend allowed on shares and deposits;
