Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 23 - Check Cashing and Deferred Deposit Lending Registration Act
********************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Check Cashing and Deferred Deposit Lending Registration Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(1): "Annual percentage rate" has the same meaning as in 15 U.S.C. Sec. 1606, as implemented by regulations issued under that section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(2): "Business of cashing checks" means cashing a check for consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(3): "Business of deferred deposit lending" means extending a deferred deposit loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(4): 70A-3-104 "Check" is as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(5): "Check casher" means a person that engages in the business of cashing checks.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(6): "Deferred deposit lender" means a person that engages in the business of deferred deposit lending.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7): (7)(a) "Deferred deposit loan" means a transaction where:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7)(a): a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7)(a)(i): presents to a deferred deposit lender a check written on that person's account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7)(a)(ii): provides written or electronic authorization to a deferred deposit lender to effect a debit from that person's account using an electronic payment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7)(b): (7)(a) the deferred deposit lender:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7)(b)(i): (7)(a) provides the person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(7)(b)(ii): agrees not to cash the check or process the debit until a specific date.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(a): "Electronic payment" means an electronic method by which a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(a)(i): accepts a payment from another person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(a)(ii): makes a payment to another person.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(b): "Electronic payment" includes a payment made through:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(b)(i): an automated clearing house transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(b)(ii): an electronic check;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(b)(iii): a stored value card; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(8)(b)(iv): an Internet transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(9): "Nationwide database" means the Nationwide Mortgage Licensing System and Registry, authorized under federal licensing requirements for mortgage loan originators.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(10): 7-23-403
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(10)(a): "Refinance" means a new deferred deposit loan transaction whose proceeds are meant to satisfy the term or amount owed on an existing deferred deposit loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(10)(b): 7-23-403 "Refinance" does not mean:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(10)(b)(i): 7-23-403 an extended payment plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(10)(b)(ii): a rollover.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-102(11): "Rollover" means the extension or renewal of the term of a deferred deposit loan.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1 Exemptions.
--------------------------------------------
The following are not subject to the requirements of this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(1): a depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(2): a depository institution holding company;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(3): an institution directly or indirectly owned or controlled by one or more:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(3)(a): depository institutions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(3)(b): depository institution holding companies; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(4): a person that cashes a check in a transaction:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(4)(a): that is incidental to a retail sale of goods or services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(4)(b): for consideration that does not exceed the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(4)(b)(i): 1% of the amount of the check; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-103.1(4)(b)(ii): $1.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-104.1 No effect on civil liability.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this chapter is intended to limit any civil liability that may exist against a check casher or deferred deposit lender for:Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-104.1(1): breach of contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-104.1(2): violation of federal law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-104.1(3): other unlawful act.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-201 Registration -- Rulemaking.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-201(1): (1)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-401(8)(c)(vi)(D): the total amount due if the person enters into an extended payment plan.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-402 Electronic disbursement and collections.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
If a deferred deposit lender collects payment on a deferred deposit loan through an electronic payment, the deferred deposit lender shall, on the day the loan is executed:Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-402(1): credit the amount of the deferred deposit loan through an electronic payment to the person receiving the deferred deposit loan; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-402(2): make the amount of the deferred deposit loan immediately available to the person receiving the deferred deposit loan.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403 Extended payment plan.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(1): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(1)(a): If a person who owes money on a deferred deposit loan requests to enter into an extended payment plan, the deferred deposit lender who extended the deferred deposit loan shall allow the person to enter into an extended payment plan that meets the requirements of this section at least once during a 12-month period to pay the money owed.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(1)(b): A deferred deposit lender is not required to enter into an extended payment plan with a person who owes money on a deferred deposit loan more than one time during a 12-month period.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(1)(c): (1) Notwithstanding the other provisions of this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(1)(c)(i): the person may request to repay the deferred deposit loan and rollovers under an extended payment plan that meets the requirements of this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(1)(c)(ii): the deferred deposit lender shall execute the extended payment plan in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2): (2)(a)(ii)(C); 7-23-401(8) An extended payment plan shall include the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a): (2)(a)(ii)(C); 7-23-401(8) A deferred deposit lender shall require a person who receives a deferred deposit loan and wants to enter an extended payment plan to enter into a written agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(i): with the deferred deposit lender;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(ii): (2)(a)(ii)(C); 7-23-401(8) that is executed:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(ii)(A): no sooner than the day before the last day of the initial term of the deferred deposit loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(ii)(B): (2)(a)(ii)(C) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(ii)(C): 7-23-401(8) for an extended payment plan offered after a default on a deferred deposit loan, 10 days after receiving the notice described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(iii): that is signed by the deferred deposit lender or its agent and the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(iv): a copy of which is given to the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(v): that states:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(v)(A): a payment schedule; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(a)(v)(B): the money owed under the extended payment plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(b): A payment schedule for an extended payment plan shall provide that the money owed may be paid:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(b)(i): in at least four equal payments; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(b)(ii): over a time period that is at least the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(b)(ii)(A): 90 days after the date of default; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(b)(ii)(B): 60 days after entering into an extended payment plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(2)(c): The money owed under an extended payment plan shall equal the money owed under the deferred deposit loan, including interest and fees, that would be due if the deferred deposit loan is paid in full on the last day of the most current term of the deferred deposit loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3): (7)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a): A deferred deposit lender may not charge interest or fees as part of an extended payment plan  regardless of the name given to the interest or fees including:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(i): an origination fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(ii): a set-up fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(iii): a collection fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(iv): a transaction fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(v): a negotiation fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(vi): a handling fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(vii): a processing fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(viii): a late fee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(a)(ix): a default fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(b): (7) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(c): A deferred deposit lender may not sell to the person who receives the deferred deposit loan any insurance or require the person to purchase insurance or any other goods or services to enter into the extended payment plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(d): A deferred deposit loan may not be considered in default during the extended payment plan period if the person who receives the deferred deposit loan complies with the terms of the extended payment plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(e): If a person who receives a deferred deposit loan defaults during the extended payment plan period, the deferred deposit lender may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(e)(i): accelerate the requirement to pay the money owed under the extended payment plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(e)(ii): charge a fee not to exceed $20;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(e)(iii): terminate the extended payment plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(3)(e)(iv): subject to the other requirements of this chapter, reinstate the original deferred deposit loan terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(4): A deferred deposit loan may not penalize a person who enters into an extended payment plan for paying to the deferred deposit lender money owed under the extended payment plan before the money is due.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(5)(a): A deferred deposit lender may not initiate collection activities for a deferred deposit loan that is subject to an extended payment plan during the period that the person owing money under the extended payment plan is in compliance with the extended payment plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(5)(b): A deferred deposit lender may not attempt to collect an amount that is greater than the amount owed under the terms of an extended payment plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(6): (3)(e)(ii); (1)(c) A deferred deposit lender may not collect additional interest or fees on a deferred deposit loan, except for the fee imposed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7): 7-23-401(5) Under an extended payment plan:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(a): a deferred deposit lender may require the person who receives a deferred deposit loan to make an initial payment of not more than 20% of the total amount due under the terms of the extended payment plan if the person has defaulted on the deferred deposit loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(b): 7-23-401(5)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(b)(i): a deferred deposit lender may require a person who receives a deferred deposit loan to provide the deferred deposit lender, as security, one or more checks or written authorizations for an electronic transfer of money that equal the total amount due under the terms of the extended payment plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(b)(ii): if the person who receives a deferred deposit loan makes a payment in the amount of a check or written authorization taken as security for that payment, the deferred deposit lender shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(b)(ii)(A): return to the person the check or written authorization stamped "void"; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(b)(ii)(B): destroy the check or written authorization; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(7)(b)(iii): 7-23-401(5) the deferred deposit lender may not charge a fee to the person who receives the deferred deposit loan for a check that is provided as security during the extended payment plan and that is not paid upon presentment if the deferred deposit lender has previously charged a fee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8): When a person who receives a deferred deposit loan makes a payment pursuant to an extended payment plan, the deferred deposit lender shall give to the person a receipt with the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8)(a): the name and address of the deferred deposit lender;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8)(b): the identification number assigned to the deferred deposit loan agreement or other information that identifies the deferred deposit loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8)(c): the date of the payment;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8)(d): the amount paid;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8)(e): the balance due on the deferred deposit loan or, when the person makes the final payment, a statement that the deferred deposit loan is paid in full; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-403(8)(f): if more than one deferred deposit loan made by the deferred deposit lender to the person is outstanding at the time the payment is made, a statement indicating to which deferred deposit loan the payment is applied.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501 Enforcement by department -- Rulemaking.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act Subject to the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1)(a): receive and act on complaints;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1)(b): take action designed to obtain voluntary compliance with this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1)(c): commence administrative or judicial proceedings on its own initiative to enforce compliance with this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1)(d): take action against a check casher or deferred deposit lender that fails to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1)(d)(i): respond to the department, in writing within 30 business days of the day on which the check casher or deferred deposit lender receives notice from the department of a complaint filed with the department; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(1)(d)(ii): submit information as requested by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(a): counsel persons and groups on their rights and duties under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act make rules in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(b)(i): restrict or prohibit lending or servicing practices that are misleading, unfair, or abusive;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(b)(ii): promote or assure fair and full disclosure of the terms and conditions of agreements and communications between a customer and:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(b)(ii)(A): a check casher; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(b)(ii)(B): a deferred deposit lender; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(b)(iii): promote or assure uniform application of or to resolve ambiguities in applicable state or federal laws or federal regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-23-501(2)(c): employ hearing examiners, clerks, and other employees and agents as necessary to perform the department's duties under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 24 - Title Lending Registration Act
***************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Title Lending Registration Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(1): "Nationwide database" means the Nationwide Mortgage Licensing System and Registry, authorized under 12 U.S.C. Sec. 5101 for federal licensing of mortgage loan originators.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(2): "Rollover" means the extension or renewal of the term of a title loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(3)(a): "Title lender" means a person that extends a title loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(3)(b): "Title lender" includes a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(3)(b)(i): arranges a title loan on behalf of a title lender;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(3)(b)(ii): acts as an agent for a title lender; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-102(3)(b)(iii): assists a title lender in the extension of a title loan.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203 Disclosure form for title loans.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2): The department shall specify by rule:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(a): the information to be provided in the disclosure form including:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(a)(i): the costs of obtaining a title loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(a)(ii): the consequences of defaulting on a title loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(a)(iii): generally available alternatives to a title loan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(a)(iv): methods of obtaining credit counseling or other financial advice;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(b): the type size of the disclosure form; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-203(2)(c): the manner in which a title lender shall conspicuously provide the disclosure form to a person seeking a title loan.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-204 Remedy for default.
--------------------------------------------------
Except in the event of fraud by a borrower, if a borrower defaults on a title loan:Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-204(1): the title lender's sole remedy is to seek repossession and sale of the property securing the title loan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-204(2): the title lender may not pursue the borrower personally for:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-204(2)(a): repayment of the loan; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-204(2)(b): any deficiency after repossession and sale of the property securing the loan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-204(3): after repossession and sale of the property securing the title loan, the title lender shall return to the borrower any proceeds from the sale in excess of the amount owed on the title loan.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301 Enforcement by department -- Rulemaking.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act Subject to the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(1)(a): receive and act on complaints;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(1)(b): take action designed to obtain voluntary compliance with this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(1)(c): commence administrative or judicial proceedings on its own initiative to enforce compliance with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2): The department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2)(a): counsel persons and groups on their rights and duties under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2)(b): make rules to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2)(b)(i): restrict or prohibit lending or servicing practices that are misleading, unfair, or abusive;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2)(b)(ii): promote or assure fair and full disclosure of the terms and conditions of agreements and communications between title lenders and customers; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2)(b)(iii): promote or assure uniform application of or to resolve ambiguities in applicable state or federal laws or federal regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-301(2)(c): employ hearing examiners, clerks, and other employees and agents as necessary to perform the department's duties under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-304 Civil liability.
-----------------------------------------------
Nothing in this chapter is intended to limit any civil liability that may exist against a title lender for:Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-304(1): breach of contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-304(2): violation of federal law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-304(3): other unlawful act.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-305 Exemptions.
------------------------------------------
The following are not subject to the requirements of this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-305(1): a depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-305(2): a depository institution holding company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-305(3): an institution directly or indirectly owned or controlled by one or more:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-305(3)(a): depository institutions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-24-305(3)(b): depository institution holding companies.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 25 - Money Transmitter Act
******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Money Transmitter Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(1): "Applicant" means a person filing an application for a license under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(2): "Authorized agent" means a person designated by the licensee under this chapter to sell or issue payment instruments or engage in the business of transmitting money on behalf of a licensee.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(3): "Blockchain" means an electronic method of storing data that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(3)(a): maintained by consensus of multiple unaffiliated parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(3)(b): distributed across multiple locations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(3)(c): mathematically verified.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(4): "Blockchain token" means an electronic record that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(4)(a): recorded on a blockchain; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(4)(b): capable of being traded between persons without an intermediary.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(5): "Executive officer" means the licensee's president, chair of the executive committee, executive vice president, treasurer, chief financial officer, or any other person who performs similar functions.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(6): "Key shareholder" means a person, or group of persons acting in concert, who is the owner of 20% or more of a class of an applicant's stock.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(7): "Licensee" means a person licensed under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(8): "Material litigation" means litigation that, according to generally accepted accounting principles, is considered significant to a person's financial health and would be required to be referenced in an annual audited financial statement, report to shareholders, or similar document.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(9)(a): "Money transmission" means the sale or issuance of a payment instrument or engaging in the business of receiving money for transmission or transmitting money within the United States or to locations abroad by any and all means, including payment instrument, wire, facsimile, or electronic transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(9)(b): "Money transmission" does not include a blockchain token.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(10): "Nationwide database" means the Nationwide Mortgage Licensing System and Registry, authorized under 12 U.S.C. Sec. 5101 for federal licensing of mortgage loan originators.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(11): "Outstanding payment instrument" means a payment instrument issued by the licensee that has been sold in the United States directly by the licensee or a payment instrument issued by the licensee that has been sold and reported to the licensee as having been sold by an authorized agent of the licensee in the United States, and that has not yet been paid by or for the licensee.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(12)(a): "Payment instrument" means a check, draft, money order, travelers check, or other instrument or written order for the transmission or payment of money, sold or issued to one or more persons, whether or not the instrument is negotiable.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(12)(b): "Payment instrument" does not include a credit card voucher, letter of credit, or instrument that is redeemable by the issuer in goods or services.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-102(13): "Remit" means either to make direct payment of the money to the licensee or its representatives authorized to receive the money, or to deposit the money in a depository institution in an account in the name of the licensee.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-103 Rules.
-------------------------------------
The commissioner may make a rule authorized by this chapter in accordance withUtah Code Annotated § 7-25-103(1): restrict or prohibit practices that are misleading, unfair, or abusive;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-103(2): promote or assure fair and full disclosure of the terms and conditions of agreements and communications between a customer and a money transmitter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-103(3): promote or assure uniform application of or to resolve ambiguities in applicable state or federal laws or federal regulations.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-201 Licensing required.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-201(1): 7-25-202 Unless exempt under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-201(2): A licensee may conduct its business in this state at one or more locations, directly or indirectly owned, or through one or more authorized agents, or both, pursuant to the single license granted to the licensee.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-202 Exemptions.
------------------------------------------
This chapter does not apply to:Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-202(1): the United States or a department or agency of the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-202(2): the state or a political subdivision of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-202(3): a depository institution or a trust company organized under the laws of a state or the United States.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203 License qualifications.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(1): An applicant for a license shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(1)(a): demonstrate, and a licensee shall maintain, a net worth of not less than $1,000,000 as demonstrated by a financial statement for the most recent fiscal year that is prepared and certified by an independent auditor and is satisfactory to the commissioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(1)(b): demonstrate experience, character, and general fitness to command the confidence of the public and warrant the belief that the business to be operated will be operated lawfully and fairly.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(2): A corporate applicant, at the time of filing of an application for a license under this chapter and at all times after a license is issued, shall be in good standing in the state of its incorporation.  A noncorporate applicant shall, at the time of the filing of an application for a license under this chapter and at all times after a license is issued, be qualified to do business in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3): Subject to the commissioner's discretion, a person may not be licensed under this chapter to do business in the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a): if the person has been convicted of, or pled guilty or no contest to, a felony:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a)(i): during the seven years preceding the day on which the individual files an application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a)(ii): at any time, if the felony involves an act of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a)(ii)(A): fraud;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a)(ii)(B): dishonesty;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a)(ii)(C): breach of trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(a)(ii)(D): money laundering; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b): if an executive officer, key shareholder, or director of the person has been convicted of, or pled guilty or no contest to, a felony:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b)(i): during the seven years preceding the day on which the individual files an application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b)(ii): at any time, if the felony involves an act of:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b)(ii)(A): fraud;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b)(ii)(B): dishonesty;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b)(ii)(C): breach of trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(3)(b)(ii)(D): money laundering.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(4): The applicant shall submit evidence satisfactory to the commissioner that the person is registered with the nationwide database.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-203(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The commissioner may by rule, made in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-205(2)(a): the applicant's business will be conducted honestly, fairly, and in a manner commanding the confidence and trust of the community;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-205(2)(b): the applicant has fulfilled the requirements imposed by this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-205(2)(c): 7-1-401 the applicant has paid the required original license fee under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206 Renewal of license.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(1): 7-25-201; 7-25-203; 7-25-204; 7-1-401 A license issued or renewed pursuant to this chapter expires on December 31.  A licensee may renew the license through the nationwide database for the ensuing 12-month period upon application by the license holder showing continued compliance with the requirements of Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The licensee shall include in its renewal application:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(2)(a): a copy of the licensee's most recent audited unconsolidated annual financial statement, including balance sheet, statement of income or loss, statement of changes in shareholder's equity, and statement of changes in financial position, except that a licensee may provide the most recent audited consolidated annual financial statement of the parent corporation if the statement separately includes the balance sheet, statement of income or loss, statement of changes in shareholder's equity, and statement of changes of financial position of the licensee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(2)(b): material changes to the information submitted by the licensee on its original application that have not previously been reported to the commissioner on any other report required to be filed under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(2)(c): a list of the locations within this state at which business regulated by this chapter is conducted by either the licensee or its authorized agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(2)(d): notification of material litigation or litigation relating to money transmission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(2)(e): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act other information the commissioner requires by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-206(3): Failure to pay the renewal fee or to submit a completed renewal application between November 1 and December 31 shall cause the license to expire at the close of business on December 31.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301 Reporting requirements.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(1): (1); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act Within 15 days of the occurrence of an event listed in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(1)(a): the filing for bankruptcy or reorganization by the licensee;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(1)(b): the institution of revocation or suspension proceedings against the licensee by a state or governmental authority with regard to the licensee's money transmission activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(1)(c): a felony indictment of the licensee or any of its officers, directors, or principals related to money transmission activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(1)(d): a felony conviction of the licensee or any of its officers, directors, or principals related to money transmission activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(1)(e): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act any other event that the commissioner may determine by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-301(2): An authorized agent shall report to the licensee the theft or loss of payment instruments valued at $5,000 or more within 24 hours from the time the authorized agent knew or should have known of the theft or loss.  Upon the receipt of the report, the licensee shall immediately provide the information to the commissioner.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-302 Changes in control of a licensee.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-302(1): A change in control of a licensee shall require prior notice to the commissioner.  In the case of a publicly traded corporation, notification shall be made in writing within 15 days of a change or acquisition of control of a licensee.  Upon notification, the commissioner may require information considered necessary to determine whether an application for a license is required.  The commissioner may waive the filing of an application if, in the commissioner's discretion, the change in control does not pose a risk to the interests of the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-302(2): Whenever control of a licensee is acquired or exercised in violation of this section, the license of the licensee shall be considered revoked as of the date of the unlawful acquisition of control.  The licensee, or its controlling person, shall surrender the license to the commissioner on demand.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-303 Authorized agent contracts.
----------------------------------------------------------
A licensee desiring to conduct licensed activities through authorized agents shall authorize each authorized agent to operate pursuant to an express written contract, which shall, at a minimum, provide the following:Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-303(1): that the licensee appoints the person as its agent with authority to sell payment instruments or transmit money on behalf of the licensee in compliance with state and federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-303(2): that neither a licensee nor an authorized agent may authorize a subagent without the written consent of the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-303(3): that licensees are subject to supervision and regulation by the commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-303(4): an acknowledgment that the authorized agent consents to the commissioner's inspection, with or without prior notice to the licensee or authorized agent, of the records of the authorized agent or agents of the licensee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-303(5): that an authorized agent is under a duty to act only as authorized under the contract with the licensee and that an authorized agent who exceeds its authority is subject to cancellation of its contract by the licensee and disciplinary action by the commissioner.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-304 Authorized agent conduct.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-304(1): An authorized agent may not make a fraudulent or false statement or misrepresentation to a licensee or to the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-304(2): A money transmission, sale, or issuance of payment instrument activity conducted by an authorized agent shall be strictly in accordance with the licensee's written procedures provided to the authorized agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-304(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act An authorized agent shall remit the money owing to the licensee in accordance with the terms of the contract between the licensee and the authorized agent.  The failure of an authorized agent to remit money owing to a licensee within the contractual time period shall result in liability of the authorized agent to the licensee for three times the licensee's actual damages.  The commissioner shall have the discretion to set, by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-304(4): The money, less fees, received by an authorized agent of a licensee from the sale or delivery of a payment instrument issued by a licensee or received by an authorized agent for transmission shall, from the time the money is received by the authorized agent until the time when the money or an equivalent amount is remitted by the authorized agent to the licensee, constitute trust funds owned by and belonging to the licensee.  If an authorized agent commingles the money with any other money or property owned or controlled by the authorized agent, the commingled proceeds and other property shall be impressed with a trust in favor of the licensee in an amount equal to the amount of the proceeds due the licensee.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-305 Instrument to bear name of licensee.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
A payment instrument issued by a licensee for sale in Utah, or which is sold in Utah, shall state on its face the name of the licensee issuer.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401 Examinations.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1): 7-1-401
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(a): The commissioner may conduct periodic on-site examinations of a licensee.  The commissioner may examine a licensee's authorized or apparent agents.  At the commissioner's discretion, written notice of the examination may be provided to the licensee or an authorized or apparent agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(b): In conducting an examination, the commissioner or the commissioner's staff:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(b)(i): shall have full and free access to all the records of the licensee and its authorized or apparent agents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(b)(ii): may summon and qualify as witnesses, under oath, and examine the directors, officers, members, agents, and employees of a licensee or authorized or apparent agent, and any other person concerning the condition and affairs of the licensee.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(c): 7-1-401 In accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(d): An on-site examination may be conducted in conjunction with examinations to be performed by representatives of agencies of another state or states.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(1)(e): The commissioner, in lieu of an on-site examination, may accept the examination report of an agency of another state, or a report prepared by an independent accounting firm, and a report so accepted is considered for all purposes as an official report of the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-401(2): 7-25-204 Upon reasonable cause, the commissioner may conduct an on-site examination of an unlicensed person to determine whether violations of this chapter have occurred or are occurring.  In conducting the examination, the commissioner has the applicable powers provided pursuant to Section

--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-402(1): 7-1-802 Information obtained by the commissioner under this chapter is confidential in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-402(2): (1) Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403 Termination or suspension of authorized agent activity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(1)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The commissioner may issue an order suspending or barring an authorized agent from continuing to be or becoming an authorized agent of a licensee during the period for which the order is in effect, if subject to
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(1)(a)(i): violated this chapter or a rule or order issued under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(1)(a)(ii): engaged or participated in an unsafe or unsound act with respect to the business of selling or issuing payment instruments of the licensee or the business of money transmission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(1)(a)(iii): made or caused to be made in an application or report filed with the commissioner or a proceeding before the commissioner, a statement that was at the time and in the circumstances under which it was made, false or misleading with respect to a material fact, or has omitted to state in the application or report a material fact that is required to be stated in the application or report.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(1)(b): Upon issuance of the order, the licensee shall terminate its relationship with the authorized agent according to the terms of the order.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-403(2): An authorized agent to whom an order is issued under this section may apply to the commissioner to modify or rescind the order.  The commissioner may not grant the application unless the commissioner finds that it is in the public interest to do so and that it is reasonable to believe that the person will, if and when the person is permitted to resume being an authorized agent of a licensee, comply with all applicable provisions of this chapter and a rule or order issued under this title.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-404 Licensee liability.
--------------------------------------------------
A licensee's responsibility to a person who purchases a payment instrument or money transmission transaction from a licensee or a licensee's authorized agent is limited to the face amount of the payment instrument or money transmission transaction purchased.

Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405 Criminal and civil penalties.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(1): A person who violates this chapter or who files materially false information with a license application or renewal under this chapter is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(1)(a): guilty of a class B misdemeanor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(1)(b): subject to revocation of the person's license under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(2): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; (2) Subject to
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(2)(a): suspend, revoke, or not renew that person's license under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(2)(b): issue a cease and desist order from committing any further violation;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(2)(c): prohibit the person from continuing to engage in the business of money transmission;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(2)(d): impose an administrative fine not to exceed $1,000 per violation, except that the aggregate total of fines imposed under this chapter against a person in a calendar year may not exceed $30,000 for that calendar year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(2)(e): (2) take any combination of actions listed under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-405(3): If the commissioner revokes a license, the department is not required to refund any portion of the licensee's filing or renewal fee for the remainder of the period for which the fee is paid.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-406 Consent orders -- Emergency order.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-406(1): The commissioner may enter into consent orders at any time with any person to resolve any matter arising under this chapter.  A consent order must be signed by the person to whom it is issued or a duly authorized representative, and must indicate agreement to the terms contained in the consent order.  A consent order need not constitute an admission by any person that any provision of this chapter, or any rule or order made or issued under this chapter, has been violated, nor need it constitute a finding by the commissioner that the person has violated any provision of this chapter or any rule or order made or issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-406(2): Notwithstanding the issuance of a consent order, the commissioner may seek civil or criminal penalties or compromise civil penalties concerning matters encompassed by the consent order.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-406(3): In cases involving extraordinary circumstances requiring immediate action, the commissioner may take any enforcement action authorized by this chapter without providing the opportunity for a prior hearing, but shall promptly afford a subsequent hearing upon an application to rescind the action taken, which is filed with the commissioner within 20 days of the receipt of the notice of the commissioner's emergency action.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-25-407 Required deposits.
-------------------------------------------------
If the commissioner finds any reasonable cause to believe that a licensee is in an unsafe or unsound condition or is unwilling or unable to pay its payment instruments when they come due, it may require the licensee to deposit funds in a financial institution acceptable to the commissioner in such amounts, for such period, and upon such conditions as the commissioner may specify, and may prohibit the licensee from issuing payment instruments for sale in Utah in an aggregate unpaid amount exceeding the amount of any such required deposit or the amount actually deposited pursuant to such a requirement, whichever is less.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 26 - Financial Exploitation Prevention Act
**********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Financial Exploitation Prevention Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(1): 26B-6-201 "Adult Protective Services" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2): "Covered financial institution" means any of the following that operate in the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a): a state or federally chartered:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(i): bank;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(ii): savings and loan association;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(iii): savings bank;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(iv): industrial bank;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(v): credit union;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(vi): trust company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(a)(vii): depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(2)(b): a financial institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(3): "Financial exploitation" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(3)(a): the wrongful or unauthorized taking, withholding, appropriation, or use of money, assets, or other property of an individual; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(3)(b): an act or omission, including through a power of attorney, guardianship, or conservatorship of an individual, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(3)(b)(i): obtain control, through deception, intimidation, or undue influence, over the individual's money, assets, or other property to deprive the individual of the ownership, use, benefit, or possession of the individual's money, assets, or other property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(3)(b)(ii): convert the individual's money, assets, or other property to deprive the individual of the ownership, use, benefit, or possession of the individual's money, assets, or other property.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(4): 53-1-102 "Law enforcement agency" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(5): "Qualified individual" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(5)(a): a branch manager of a covered financial institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(5)(b): a director, officer, employee, agent, or other representative that a covered financial institution designates.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(6): "Third party associated with a vulnerable adult" means an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(6)(a): who is a parent, spouse, adult child, sibling, or other known family member of a vulnerable adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(6)(b): whom a vulnerable adult authorizes the financial institution to contact;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(6)(c): who is a co-owner, additional authorized signatory, or beneficiary on a vulnerable adult's account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(6)(d): who is an attorney, trustee, conservator, guardian or other fiduciary whom a court or a government agency selects to manage some or all of the financial affairs of the vulnerable adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7): 61-1-3 "Transaction" means any of the following services that a covered financial institution provides:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(a): a transfer or request to transfer or disburse funds or assets in an account;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(b): a request to initiate a wire transfer, initiate an automated clearinghouse transfer, or issue a money order, cashier's check, or official check;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(c): a request to negotiate a check or other negotiable instrument;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(d): a request to change the ownership of, or access to, an account;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(e): 61-1-3 a request to sell or transfer a security or other asset, or a request to affix a medallion stamp or provide any form of guarantee or endorsement in connection with an attempt to sell or transfer a security or other asset, if the person selling or transferring the security or asset is not required to obtain a license under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(f): a request for a loan, extension of credit, or draw on a line of credit;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(g): a request to encumber any movable or immovable property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(7)(h): a request to designate or change the designation of beneficiaries to receive any property, benefit, or contract right.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(8): 26B-6-201 "Vulnerable adult" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(8)(a): an individual who is 65 years old or older; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-102(8)(b): 26B-6-201 the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201 Permitted delay of wire transfers.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(1): This section applies to a wire transfer that transfers money from a consumer account at a covered financial institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(2): If a qualified individual reasonably believes that executing a requested wire transfer will result in financial exploitation, the covered financial institution may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(2)(a): delay the wire transfer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(2)(b): contact:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(2)(b)(i): a law enforcement agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(2)(b)(ii): Adult Protective Services; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(2)(b)(iii): a joint co-owner on the account.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(3): (2) The delay of a wire transfer described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(3)(a): the covered financial institution reasonably determines that the wire transfer is not financial exploitation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-201(3)(b): 15 business days pass after the day on which the covered financial institution first initiated the delay of the wire transfer.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-202 Office of the Attorney General website.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
The Office of the Attorney General shall post on the Office of the Attorney General's website up-to-date information regarding financial scams, including:Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-202(1): the most prominent and common characteristics of financial scams;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-202(2): current or trending financial scams;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-202(3): resources for a vulnerable adult who suspects a financial scam; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-202(4): resources for an individual who suspects the financial exploitation of a vulnerable adult.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301 Delay of a transaction involving a vulnerable adult.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(1): A covered financial institution may delay a transaction involving a vulnerable adult, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(1)(a): a qualified individual reasonably believes that executing the requested transaction will result in financial exploitation of the vulnerable adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(1)(b): a law enforcement agency provides the covered financial institution information demonstrating that it is reasonable to believe that financial exploitation of a vulnerable adult is occurring, has or may have occurred, is being attempted, or has been or may have been attempted.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2): (1); (2)(b); (2)(a)(i); (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a): (1); (2)(b) A covered financial institution that delays a transaction in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a)(i): (2)(b) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a)(i)(A): authorized to transact business on the account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a)(i)(B): for which the covered financial institution has contact information;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a)(ii): may send notice of the delay, the reason for the delay, or any additional information about the transaction to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a)(ii)(A): a law enforcement agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(a)(ii)(B): Adult Protective Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(b): (2)(a)(i); (2)(a) A covered financial institution may:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(b)(i): (2)(a)(i) decide not to provide notice to a party described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(2)(b)(ii): (2)(a) send a notice described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3): (3)(b); (1); (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(a): (3)(b); (1) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(a)(i): the covered financial institution reasonably determines that the transaction will not result in financial exploitation of a vulnerable adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(a)(ii): 15 business days pass after the day on which the covered financial institution first initiated the delay of the transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(b): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(b)(i): (3)(a) If a covered financial institution receives a request from a law enforcement agency to extend the delay of a transaction beyond the expiration date established in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(b)(ii): A court of competent jurisdiction may enter an order:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(b)(ii)(A): extending or shortening the delay of a transaction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-301(3)(b)(ii)(B): providing relief based on the petition of the covered financial institution, law enforcement agency, or an interested party.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-302 Permitted notifications.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-302(1): A covered financial institution may notify a law enforcement agency or Adult Protective Services if a qualified individual believes that the financial exploitation of a vulnerable adult is occurring, has or may have occurred, is being attempted, or has been or may have been attempted.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-302(2): A covered financial institution may notify a third party associated with a vulnerable adult if a qualified individual believes that the financial exploitation of the vulnerable adult is occurring, has or may have occurred, is being attempted, or has been or may have been attempted.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-302(3): (2) A covered financial institution may choose not to notify a third party associated with a vulnerable adult as described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401 Immunity.
----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(1): A covered financial institution or a director, officer, employee, attorney, accountant, agent, or other representative of the covered financial institution:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(1)(a): has no duty to act under this chapter to protect a vulnerable adult from financial exploitation by a third person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(1)(b): is immune from all criminal, civil, and administrative liability for not taking a permissive action under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(2): 7-26-201(2); 7-26-301; 7-26-302 A covered financial institution or a director, officer, employee, attorney, accountant, agent, or other representative of the covered financial institution who chooses to act as described in:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(2)(a): 7-26-201(2) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(2)(b): 7-26-301; 7-26-302 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(2)(b)(i): is done in bad faith; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(2)(b)(ii): causes pecuniary loss to a vulnerable adult suspected of being a victim of financial exploitation.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-26-401(3): The immunity described in this section does not extend to an individual that is a principal, a conspirator, or an accessory after the fact to a criminal offense involving the financial exploitation of a vulnerable adult.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 7 - Chapter 27 - Commercial Financing Registration and Disclosure Act
*************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(1): 70A-9a-102; 70A-9a-102 "Accounts receivable purchase transaction" means a transaction in which a business forwards or otherwise sells to a person all or a portion of the business's accounts, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(2): "Broker" means a person who, for compensation or the expectation of compensation, arranges a commercial financing transaction between a third party and a business in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(3): "Business" means a private enterprise carried on for the purpose of gain or economic profit.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(4)(a): "Business purpose transaction" means a transaction from which the resulting proceeds that a business receives are:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(4)(a)(i): provided to the business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(4)(a)(ii): intended to be used to carry on the business.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(4)(b): "Business purpose transaction" does not include a transaction from which the resulting proceeds are intended to be used for personal, family, or household purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(4)(c): For purposes of determining whether a transaction is a business purpose transaction, a provider may rely on a written statement of intended purpose, signed by an individual authorized to sign on behalf of the business. The written statement may be contained in an application, agreement, or other document signed by an individual authorized to sign on behalf of the business.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(5): "Commercial financing transaction" means a business purpose transaction:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(5)(a): under which a person extends a business a commercial loan or a commercial open-end credit plan; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(5)(b): that is an accounts receivable purchase transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(6): "Commercial loan" means a loan to a business, regardless of whether the loan is secured.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(7): "Commercial open-end credit plan" means commercial financing extended to a business on terms under which:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(7)(a): the creditor reasonably contemplates repeat transactions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(7)(b): subject to any limit set by the creditor, the amount of financing that the creditor may extend to the business during the term of the plan is made available to the extent that any outstanding balance is repaid.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(8): 41-3-102 "Motor vehicle dealer" means a dealer as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(9)(a): "Provider" means a person who consummates more than five commercial financing transactions in the state during any calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-101(9)(b): "Provider" includes a person who, under a written agreement with a depository institution, offers one or more commercial financing products provided by the depository institution via an online platform that the person administers.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102 Application.
-------------------------------------------
The provisions of this chapter do not apply to:Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(1): a provider that is a depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(2): a provider that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(2)(a)(i): a subsidiary of a depository institution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(2)(a)(ii): a service corporation for a depository institution; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(2)(b): regulated by a federal banking agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(3): a provider that is regulated under the federal Farm Credit Act 12 U.S.C. Sec. 2001 et seq.;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(4): Chapter 25, Money Transmitter Act a provider that is licensed as a money transmitter in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(5): a provider that consummates five or fewer commercial financing products in the state during any 12 month period;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(6): a commercial financing transaction secured by real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(7): 70A-2a-103 a commercial financing transaction that is a lease as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(8): 70A-9a-103 a commercial financing transaction that is a purchase-money obligation as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(9): 13-48-103 a commercial financing transaction that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(9)(a): involves a commercial loan or a commercial open-end credit plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(9)(b): is $50,000 or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(9)(c): 13-48-103 extends the commercial loan or the commercial open-end credit plan to:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(9)(c)(i): a motor vehicle dealer or the motor vehicle dealer's affiliate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(9)(c)(ii): 13-48-103 a motor vehicle rental company as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(10): a commercial financing transaction offered by a person in connection with the sale of a product or service that:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(10)(a): the person manufactures, licenses, or distributes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(10)(b): the person's parent company or the person's owned and controlled subsidiary manufactures, licenses, or distributes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-102(11): a commercial financing transaction of more than $1,000,000.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-201 Registration requirements -- Rulemaking.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-201(1)(a): Beginning January 1, 2023, it is unlawful for a person to engage in a commercial financing transaction as a provider in Utah or with a Utah resident, unless the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-201(1)(a)(i): registers with the department in accordance with this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-201(1)(a)(ii): maintains a valid registration.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-201(1)(b): An officer or employee of a person required to register under this section is not required to register if the person for whom the individual is an officer or employee is registered.

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(1)(a): Before consummating a commercial financing transaction, a provider shall disclose the terms of the commercial financing transaction in accordance with this section and rules made by the commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(1)(b): (1)(a) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(1)(b)(i): after any disbursement of funds that occurs after the parties consummate the commercial financing transaction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(1)(b)(ii): no later than 15 days after the last day of the calendar month in which the disbursement of funds occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2): (2)(a); (2)(a); (2)(c); (2)(a) A provider shall disclose the following information in connection with each commercial financing transaction:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(a): the total amount of funds provided to the business under the terms of the commercial financing transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(b): (2)(a) the total amount of funds disbursed to the business under the terms of the commercial financing transaction, if less than the amount described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(c): the total amount to be paid to the provider under the terms of the commercial financing transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(d): (2)(a); (2)(c) the total dollar cost of the commercial financing transaction, calculated by finding the difference between:
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(d)(i): (2)(a) the amount described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(d)(ii): (2)(c) the amount described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(e)(i): the manner, frequency, and amount of each payment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(e)(ii): if the amount of each payment may vary, the manner, frequency, and estimated amount of the initial payment;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(f): a statement of whether there are any costs or discounts associated with prepayment under the commercial financing transaction, including a reference to the paragraph in the commercial financing transaction agreement that creates each cost or discount; and
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(2)(g): (2)(a) any amount of the funds described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(3): The commercial financing transaction agreement shall include a description of the methodology for calculating any variable payment amount and the circumstances that may cause a payment amount to vary.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-202(4): The provisions of this section apply to a commercial financing transaction consummated on or after January 1, 2023.


Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301 Penalties.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act Subject to the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(1)(a): receive and act on complaints;
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(1)(b): take action designed to obtain voluntary compliance with this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(1)(c): commence administrative or judicial proceedings on the department's own initiative to enforce compliance with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(2): A person who violates a provision of this chapter is subject to a civil penalty of $500 per violation, not to exceed $20,000 for all violations arising from the use of the same transaction documentation or materials.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(3): A person who violates a provision of this chapter after receiving written notice of a prior violation is subject to a civil penalty of $1,000 per violation, not to exceed $50,000 for all violations arising from the use of the same transaction documentation or materials.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(4): Nothing in this chapter creates a private right of action against any person based on failure to comply with the provisions of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 7-27-301(5): A violation of this chapter does not affect the enforceability of any underlying agreement.
